Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Women's Congregation and Their Imam
Commentary on the ruling of women praying in congregation with a female imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregation, explain the required positioning of the female imam, and identify the hadith evidence that discourages women from attending congregational prayers.

Core Idea
Women's congregation with a female imam is makruh tahrimi; if performed, the imam must stand in the middle of the row.

The Hanafi school carefully regulates women's participation in congregational prayer, balancing the virtue of congregation with the higher virtue of concealment for women. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the ruling, the required positioning of a female imam, and the evidence from the Prophet's hadith. By understanding this, you will see how the school prioritizes privacy and avoidance of fitna while still validating the prayer if performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is women forming a congregation with a female imam. The ruling is makruh tahrimi (severely disliked). Determine what 'makruh tahrimi' means and why it is applied here: because it necessitates one of two disliked actions (imam in first row or imam advancing).
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; the act is sinful but the prayer is valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith: 'A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her room, and her prayer in her innermost chamber is better than her prayer in her house.' This indicates that more concealment is better for women's prayer.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) and zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The comparative 'afdal' (better) implies that privacy is superior. Therefore, attending congregation (which is less private) is less virtuous. The Hanafi school uses this to discourage women from attending mosques and from forming their own congregations.
The ruling is not absolute prohibition but strong discouragement.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) permit women's congregation without dislike, especially if no men are present. The Hanafi position is based on the necessity of proper positioning: the imam must stand in the middle, which is itself disliked.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi view is mufta bihi in the school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is makruh tahrimi, but if performed, the imam must stand in the middle of the row (with heels slightly forward). Later scholars (mutakhkhirin) affirmed this, and it is based on the hadith and the principle of avoiding fitna.
The ruling also allows women to be led by a man without dislike, except in certain domestic settings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) كره جماعة (النساء) بواحدة منهن ولا يحضرن الجماعات لما فيه من الفتنة والمخالفة فإن فعلن ) يجب أن يقف الإمام وسطهن) مع تقدم عقبها فلو تقدمت كالرجال أثمت وصحت الصلاة، والإمام من يؤتم به ذكراً كان أو أنثى، والوسط بالتحريك ما بين طرفي الشيء كما هنا وبالسكون لما لا صبي يبين بعضه ما أفتى به المتأخرون أفاد السيد، وقال البدر العيني : يجوز الاقتداء بالمخالف، وكل بر وفاجر ما لم يكن مبتدعاً بدعة يكفر بها، وما لم يتحقق من إمامه مفسداً لصلاته في إعتقاده اهـ، وإذا لم يجد غير المخالف فلا كراهة في الاقتداء به والاقتداء به أولى من الإنفراد على أن الكراهة تنافي الثواب أفاده العلامة نوح قوله: (وكره) جماعة (النساء) تحريماً للزوم أحد المحظورين قيام الإمام في الصف الأول وهو مكروه، أو تقدم الإمام وهو أيضاً مكروه، في حقهن سيد عن الدرر، ولو أمهن رجل، فلا كراهة إلا أن يكون في بيت ليس معهن فيه رجل، أو محرم من الإمام أو زوجته فإن كان واحد ممن ذكر معهن فلا كراهة كما لو كان في المسجد مطلقاً. قوله: (ولا يحضرن الجماعات لقوله : صلاة المرأة في بيتها أفضل من صلاتها في حجرتها وصلاتها في مخدعها أفضل من صلاتها في بيتها اهـ فالأفضل لها ما كان أستر لها لا فرق بين الفرائض، وغيرها كالتراويح إلا صلاة الجنازة فلا تكره جماعتهن فيها لأنها لم تشرع مكررة فلو انفردت تفوتهن، ولو أمت المرأة في صلاة الجنازة رجالاً لا تعاد لسقوط الفرض بصلاتها.
(And) he disliked the congregation of (women) with one of them (as imam), and they should not attend congregations because of the fitna and opposition (to the command). If they do (perform congregational prayer), it is obligatory that the imam stands in the middle of them, with her heel advanced. If she advances like men, she sins but the prayer is valid. The imam is the one followed, whether male or female. 'Al-wasat' with fatha means what is between the two ends of something, as here; with sukun, it is used when it does not separate parts. This is what the later scholars gave fatwa on, as reported by al-Sayyid. Al-Badr al-'Ayni said: It is permissible to follow a person of a different madhhab, every pious or sinful person, as long as he is not an innovator of kufr-disbelief, and as long as the follower does not believe that his imam's prayer is invalid. If he finds no one except a mukhalif, there is no dislike in following him, and following him is better than praying alone, even though dislike negates reward (this is from Allama Nuh). His statement: (And he disliked) congregation of (women) meaning it is severely disliked because it necessitates one of two prohibitions: either the imam stands in the first row (which is disliked) or she advances (which is also disliked) – in their case, as reported from al-Sayyid from al-Durar. If a man leads them, there is no dislike, unless they are in a house with no man present besides the imam or his wife. If one of those mentioned is with them, there is no dislike, just as if they were in a mosque unconditionally. His statement: (And they should not attend congregations) because of his statement: 'A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her room, and her prayer in her innermost chamber is better than her prayer in her house.' So the best for her is what is most concealing, whether obligatory or supererogatory like tarawih, except for funeral prayer: their congregation is not disliked because it is not repeated; if they pray individually, they would miss it. If a woman leads men in funeral prayer, it is not repeated because the obligation is fulfilled by her prayer.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage covers several related rulings. First, it is makruh tahrimi for women to form a congregation with a female imam, because it forces either the imam to stand in the first row (disliked) or to advance forward (also disliked). If they do so, the imam must stand in the middle of the row, with her heels ahead of the others; if she stands like a male imam (ahead), she sins but the prayer is valid. The passage then discusses that following a mukhalif (someone of a different madhhab) is permissible except for those who hold kufr beliefs. For women, the best is to pray alone in the most concealed place, except for funeral prayer where congregation is recommended to avoid missing it. A woman can lead a funeral prayer for men, and it is valid.

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasat): In this context, the position where the imam stands in the middle of the row, between the two ends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should a female imam stand when leading women in prayer?
A) In front of the first row like a man.
B) In the middle of the row, level with the followers.
C) At the back of the congregation.
D) Alone in a separate room.

Key Takeaway
Women's congregation with a female imam is makruh tahrimi, but if performed, the imam must stand in the middle of the row and the prayer is valid.

Positioning of a Single Follower and Multiple Followers
Fiqh ruling with proof on follower positioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct position for a single follower in Hanafi congregational prayer, identify the evidence from the Sunnah, and distinguish sunnah from makruh positioning.

Core Idea
A single follower stands to the imam's right, level with him; the hadith of Ibn Abbas establishes this sunnah.

When praying in congregation, where a follower stands relative to the imam is not random—it follows a sunnah established by the Prophet's practice. This lesson, from al-Tahtawi's hashia on Maraqi al-Falah, clarifies the exact positioning for one or more followers, resolving minor intra-Hanafi differences and citing the key hadith. Understanding this ruling ensures your congregational prayer aligns with the preferred practice of the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act being ruled upon is where a single male follower (or discerning boy) stands relative to the imam. The ruling is that standing to the right, level with the imam, is sunnah; standing to the left or directly behind is makruh tanzih.
The prayer is valid even if the follower stands elsewhere, but the sunnah is missed.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas, who stood to the left of the Prophet during prayer, and the Prophet moved him to the right. This indicates the correct position.
The hadith is ahad (singular transmission) but accepted for establishing sunnah.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of moving Ibn Abbas from left to right demonstrates that the right side is the prescribed place for a single follower. It also shows that the follower should not be behind the imam (the Prophet turned him from behind).
This is a clear indication (dalalah zanniyya) but sufficient for the ruling.
4
Note the dislike for left and behind
The text explicitly states that standing to the left or behind the imam is makruh (disliked). The phrase 'in the sound view' (fi al-sahih) confirms this position.
Some early texts had conflicting reports; the hashia resolves it in favor of the sound view.
5
Apply the ruling for multiple followers
When there are two or more followers, they stand behind the imam in rows, with the first row being directly behind. The text provides detailed ordering.
The standing of multiple followers forms a separate set of rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويقف الواحد) رجلاً كان أو صبياً مميزاً عن يمين (الإمام) مساوياً له متأخراً بعقبه ويكره أن يقف عن يساره، وكذا خلفه في الصحيح لحديث ابن عباس أنه قام عن يسار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فأقامه عن يمينه (و) يقف (الأكثر ) من واحد خلفه لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام تقدم عن أنس، واليتيم أن يقول في الثاني، وبالسكون لما كان داخل الشيء، أو يقول في الأول والوسط بالتحريك اسم لما يبين بعضه عن بعض وبالسكون ما بين طرفي الشيء، وفي السيد عن الصحاح كل موضع صلح فيه بين فبالتسكين كجسلت وسط القوم وإلا فبالتحريك كجلست وسط الدار، وربما سكن وليس بالوجه اهـ وقيل كل منهما يقع موقع الآخر . قال ابن الأثير : وكأنه الأشبه نهر اهـ. قوله: (ويمد كل منهم رجليه كذا في الذخيرة والأولى ما في منية المصلى من قوله : يقعد كما في الصلاة فعلى هذا الرجل يفترش وهي تتورك لأنه يحصل به من المبالغة في الستر ما لا يحصل في الهيئة المذكورة مع خلو هذه الهيئة عن مد الرجل إلى القبلة من غير ضرورة بحر ونهر اهـ ذكره السيد قوله : ( ويقف الواحد) أما الواحدة فتتأخر إلا إذا اقتدت بمثلها، وإذا عن يمينه وأقامها خلفه . قوله : متأخراً بعقبه في كلامه تعارض والذي في شروح الهداية، والقدوري والكنز والبرهان والقهستاني أنه يقف مساوياً له بدون تقدم وبدون تأخر من غير فرجة في ظاهر الرواية، وهذا إذا كان قبل الصلاة فإن كان فيها أشار إليه بيده ليحاذيه. قوله : (في الصحيح راجع إلى قوله وكذا خلفه فقط، ولذا فصله بقوله، وكذا وعن يضع أصابعه عند عقب الإمام. قوله: الحديث ابن عباس الخ) في الحديث دلالة على جواز صلاة النافلة بالجماعة وإن العمل القليل لا يبطل الصلاة، وأنه لا يجوز تقدم المأموم على الإمام لأن النبي أداره من وراء ظهره، وكانت إدارته من بين يديه أيسر وأنه يجوز الصلاة خلفه وإن لم ينو الإمامة لأن النبي شرع في صلاته منفرداً، ثم انتم به ابن عباس وأن صلاة الصبي صحيحة وأن له موقفاً من الإمام كالبالغ وأنه ينبغي للإمام إرشاد المأموم إلى السنة كذا في شروح الحديث . قوله : (ويقف الأكثر من (واحد صادق بالاثنين وكيفيته أن يقف واحد بحذائه والآخر عن يمينه، ولو جاء واحد وقف عن يسار الأول الذي هو بحذاء الإمام فيصير الإمام متوسطاً، ويقف الرابع عن يمين الواقف الذي هو عن يمين من بحذاء الإمام والخامس عن يسار الثالث، وهكذا فإذا استوى الجانبان يقوم الجائي عن جهة اليمين وأن ترجح اليمين يقوم عن يسار قهستاني، وفي العتابية لو قام الإمام وسط القوم أو قاموا هم عن يمينه، أو عن يساره أساؤا اهـ وفي الفتح عن الدراية ولو قام واحد بجنب الإمام وخلفه صف كره إجماعاً وروي عن الإمام أنه قال : أكره للإمام أن يقوم بين الساريتين أو في زاوية أو ناحية المسجد، أو إلى سارية لأنه
His statement: (And the one person stands) whether a man or a discerning boy, to the right of the imam, level with him, with his heel slightly behind. It is disliked for him to stand to the left, and likewise behind him, on the sound view, due to the hadith of Ibn Abbas: he stood to the left of the Prophet (peace be upon him), so he moved him to his right. (And) the majority (more than one) stand behind him, because he (peace be upon him) advanced, according to Anas and the orphan... (then discussion of the word 'wasat') ... His statement: (And each of them extends his legs) as in al-Dhakhira; the better view is from Munyat al-Musalli that he sits as in prayer. Thus the man sits iftirash and the woman tawarruk, because it achieves greater covering... His statement: (And the one stands) while a woman stands behind unless led by a woman... As for 'with his heel behind', there is a contradiction; in the commentaries of al-Hidayah, al-Quduri, al-Kanz, etc., he stands level without being forward or backward, with no gap in the apparent riwayah. This applies before the prayer; if during the prayer, he signals with his hand to align. His statement: ('in the sahih' refers only to 'and likewise behind him', so he separated it with 'and likewise'...) The hadith of Ibn Abbas indicates the permissibility of supererogatory prayer in congregation, that a small action does not invalidate the prayer, that the follower must not advance ahead of the imam (because the Prophet turned him from behind his back), and that it is permissible to pray behind someone who did not intend to lead (because the Prophet started his prayer alone, then Ibn Abbas joined him). It also indicates that a boy's prayer is valid and that he has a standing position like an adult, and that the imam should guide the follower to the Sunnah. His statement: (And the majority stands) of more than one: it is true for two, and its manner is that one stands opposite him and the other to his right. If another comes, he stands to the left of the first who is opposite the imam, making the imam in the middle. The fourth stands to the right of the one who is to the right of the one opposite the imam, and the fifth to the left of the third, and so on. When both sides are equal, the newcomer stands on the right side; if the right is already heavier, he stands on the left (Qahistani). In al-Atabiyya: if the imam stands in the middle of the people or they all stand to his right or left, they have done wrong. In al-Fath from al-Diraya: if one stands next to the imam and behind him there is a row, it is disliked by consensus. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that he said: I dislike for the imam to stand between two pillars or in a corner or a side of the mosque, or next to a pillar because...
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on the positioning of followers relative to the imam in congregational prayer. A single follower (male or discerning child) stands to the right of the imam, level with him, slightly behind with his heel. Standing to the left or directly behind is disliked. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas whom the Prophet moved from left to right. When there are two or more followers, they stand behind the imam in rows. The text then discusses the manner of forming rows, with the first standing opposite the imam, the second to his right, and subsequent rows filling in a specific order. It also mentions that a woman follower stands behind, unless the imam is also a woman. The commentary resolves a contradiction regarding the exact position of the single follower: the preferred view is that he stands exactly level without being forward or backward, in line with the zahir al-riwayah. Additional rulings include the dislike of the imam standing in certain positions within the mosque.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yamin): The right side of the imam; the place for a single male follower.
مساوياً (musawiyan): Level with the imam in terms of forward positioning; the follower's heel should be slightly behind, but the body should be aligned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of Ibn Abbas, why did the Prophet (peace be upon him) move him from the left to the right?
A) To demonstrate that the right side is the only valid place for a follower.
B) To teach that a single follower must not stand behind the imam.
C) To establish the sunnah of standing on the right for a single follower.
D) Because Ibn Abbas was a child and the Prophet wanted him to be on his right.

Key Takeaway
A single male follower stands to the imam's right, level with him, as proven by the hadith of Ibn Abbas; deviation is makruh tanzih but the prayer remains valid.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Position of a Single Follower in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on the position of a single male follower with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a single male follower's position in prayer and apply the hadith proof to determine the correct placement.

Core Idea
A single follower stands to the imam's right; left or behind is discouraged.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the position of a single male follower in congregational prayer. The ruling is based on a well-known hadith of Ibn Abbas. Understanding this sunnah position helps ensure that prayer is performed in accordance with the best practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the placement of a single male follower (or discerning boy) relative to the imam. The ruling: standing to the right is sunnah; standing to the left or behind is makruh tanzih.
The hukm distinguishes between preferred (sunnah) and disliked (makruh).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas, recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim. He stood to the left of the Prophet ﷺ, and the Prophet moved him to the right.
This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of moving Ibn Abbas indicates that the right side is the preferred position for a single follower. The imperative implication (amr) leads to sunnah, not obligation.
The fiqhi principle: the Prophet's action is a proof (fi'l) that indicates recommendation.
4
Note the details of the position
The follower stands level with the imam but slightly behind with his heel. This ensures alignment without stepping ahead of the imam.
Equality in standing is important; the slight offset prevents the follower from being ahead.
5
Evaluate cross-madhhab difference
The Maliki school allows a follower to stand to the left if there is no space on the right. The Hanafi position remains that right is sunnah and left is makruh, even if space is limited.
This difference has practical implications in crowded masjids.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقف الواحد رجلاً كان أو صبياً مميزاً عن يمين الإمام مساوياً له متأخراً بعقبه ويكره أن يقف عن يساره وكذا خلفه في الصحيح لحديث ابن عباس أنه قام عن يسار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فأقامه عن يمينه
And the single person, whether a man or a discerning boy, stands to the right of the imam, level with him, slightly behind with his heel, and it is disliked for him to stand to his left, and likewise behind him according to the correct view, due to the hadith of Ibn Abbas that he stood to the left of the Prophet (peace be upon him) so he moved him to his right.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a single male follower (or a discerning boy) in congregational prayer. Such a follower must stand to the imam's right, level with him but slightly behind (with his heel at the imam's heel). Standing to the imam's left or behind him is disliked (makruh) according to the correct view. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas, who initially stood to the left of the Prophet ﷺ during night prayer, and the Prophet moved him to his right. This indicates the preferred position.

Key Terms
مميز (mumayyiz): A child who has reached the age of discernment (usually around 7 years) and can understand the meaning of prayer and respond to the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should a single male follower stand in relation to the imam?
A) To the left of the imam
B) To the right of the imam
C) Directly behind the imam
D) Anywhere in the row

Key Takeaway
A single male follower should stand to the right of the imam, as shown by the Prophet's practice.

Multiple Followers Stand Behind the Imam
Ruling on the position of two or more followers in congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred position for two or more followers in congregational prayer and explain the Hanafi evidence from the hadith of Anas and the orphan.

Core Idea
When two or more follow the imam, they stand behind him; standing beside is merely permissible.

In congregational prayer, the positioning of followers relative to the imam depends on their number. For a single follower, standing to the imam's right is sunnah. When there are two or more, the preferred arrangement changes. The classical Hanafi text explains this rule and supports it with a clear proof from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states: 'Those who are more than one stand behind him.' The condition 'more than one' means two or more followers. The ruling is that they should stand behind the imam.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith that the Prophet stepped forward when praying with Anas and the orphan, indicating that multiple followers stand behind the imam. This action is evidence of preference (afdaliyya).
The hadith is recorded in Sahih Muslim.
3
Distinguish between preference and permissibility
The passage also notes that a narration about standing between the imam (i.e., beside him) is evidence of permissibility (ibaha), not preference. Thus, standing behind is sunnah muakkadah; standing beside is allowed but less preferred.
This distinction prevents misunderstanding that both options are equal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقف الأكثر من واحد خلفه لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام تقدم عن أنس واليتيم حين صلى بهما وهو دليل الأفضلية وما ورد من القيام بينهما فهو دليل الإباحة
And those who are more than one stand behind him because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stepped forward when he prayed with Anas and the orphan (Yateem), and this is evidence of preference; and what has been narrated about standing between them is evidence of permissibility.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage addresses the position of multiple followers (two or more). They stand behind the imam, forming a row or rows behind him. The proof is the hadith that when the Prophet prayed with Anas and the orphan boy (Yateem), he stepped forward, making them stand behind him. This indicates that the preferred arrangement is for multiple followers to be behind the imam. There is also a narration of Ibn Mas'ud standing between Alqama and Aswad, which indicates permissibility (ibahah) but not preference. The preferred way is behind.

Key Terms
الأكثر (al-akthar): Literally 'more than one', meaning two or more followers. Technically, it refers to multiple followers as opposed to a single follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred position for two or more followers in congregational prayer?
A) One on each side of the imam
B) Both behind the imam
C) One behind and one on the right
D) Any arrangement is equally good

Key Takeaway
For two or more followers, the sunnah is to stand behind the imam; standing beside is permissible but not preferred.

Rulings on Aligning Rows and Imam's Position
Commentary on prayer row etiquettes with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on row alignment, identify the proofs from hadith, and apply the rulings when encountering gaps or needing to adjust rows during congregational prayer.

Core Idea
Aligning rows and touching shoulders is a sunnah, not hypocrisy—it is obedience to the Prophet's command.

This lesson delves into the etiquettes of congregational prayer rows as detailed in the Hanafi tradition. We will examine the proofs from the Prophet's commands regarding straightening rows, filling gaps, and the proper response to those who may hesitate to adjust for fear of ostentation. The goal is to understand the legal rulings and the wisdom behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key hadith
List the three hadith cited: (1) 'Let those with understanding stand near me', (2) 'Be straight, your hearts will become straight, and touch each other', (3) 'Whoever connects a row, Allah will connect him'. Note their content and chain.
All are ahad hadith, so they indicate sunnah, not obligation.
2
Understand the Hanafi position
From the hadith, the Hanafi school rules that aligning rows and touching shoulders is sunnah mu'akkadah. The imam should instruct the rows. Leaving gaps is makruh.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the refuted misconception
Some think making space or touching is riya' (showing off). The text refutes this, stating it is assistance in obedience. Understand why it is not hypocrisy: it is a small act done for Allah and His Messenger.
The action is not for show but to comply with the Sunnah.
4
Apply rulings to scenarios
Scenario 1: Gap in first row but not second → break through to fill. Scenario 2: Row organized but waiting, fear missing rak'ah → pull a knowledgeable person who won't be annoyed, else pray alone. This refutes the view that making space invalidates prayer.
Pulling is allowed as a minor movement.
5
Confirm virtue of front rows
The best rows are the first, then the nearest, based on hadith that mercy descends on the imam then those aligned with him.
This encourages rushing to the front.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصف الرجال لقوله : ليلتي منكم أولو الأحلام والنهي فيأمرهم الإمام بذلك، وقال : استووا تستو قلوبكم وتماسوا تراحموا وقال : أقيموا الصفوف وحاذوا بين المناكب وسدوا الخلل ولينوا بأيديكم إخوانكم لا تذروا فرجات للشيطان من وصل صفا وصله الله، ومن قطع صفا قطعه الله وبهذا يعلم جهل من يستمسك عند دخول أحد بجنبه في الصف يظن أنه رياء، بل هو إعانة على ما أمر به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وإذا وجد فرجة في الصف الأول دون الثاني فله خرقه لتركهم سد الأول، ولو كان الصف منتظماً ينتظر مجيء آخر فإن خاف فوت الركعة جذب عالماً بالحكم لا يتأذى به وإلا قام وحده وهذه ترد القول بفساد من فسح لامرىء داخل بجنبه، وأفضل الصفوف أولها ، ثم الأقرب فالأقرب لما روي أن الله تعالى ينزل الرحمة أولا على الإمام، ثم تتجاوز عنه إلى من يحاذيه في الصف الأول، ثم إلى
And he arranges the men due to his statement: 'Let stand nearest to me those with understanding and intelligence,' so the imam commands them to do that. And he said: 'Be straight, your hearts will become straight, and touch each other, you will receive mercy.' And he said: 'Straighten the rows, align between the shoulders, fill the gaps, and soften your hands for your brothers. Do not leave gaps for the devil. Whoever connects a row, Allah will connect him; and whoever cuts a row, Allah will cut him off.' And by this, one knows the ignorance of one who holds back when someone enters beside him in the row, thinking it is hypocrisy, rather it is assistance in what the Prophet commanded. And if there is a gap in the first row but not in the second, he may break through because they neglected to fill the first. If the row is organized waiting for another to come, but he fears missing the rak'ah, he may pull someone who knows the ruling and will not be disturbed; otherwise he prays alone. This refutes the statement that someone who makes space for one entering beside him invalidates his prayer. And the best of rows are the first, then the nearer (to the front), because it is narrated that Allah sends mercy first upon the imam, then it goes from him to those aligned with him in the first row, then to...
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This is a critical refinement passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, commenting on the rulings and etiquettes of prayer rows. The author begins by affirming that the imam should arrange the men, citing the hadith 'Let those with understanding and intelligence stand nearest to me' to show that the most deserving should be in the front. He then lists several commands from the Prophet regarding row alignment: straightening the rows aligns hearts, touching shoulders fosters mercy, filling gaps prevents Satan from entering, and encouraging others gently is a help, not hypocrisy. The author addresses a common misunderstanding: some hesitate to touch others' shoulders when entering a row, thinking it is showing off; but this is actually compliance with the Prophet's order. If a gap exists in the first row but not the second, one may break through the second row to fill the first, as those in the first row neglected their duty. If the row is full but waiting for a latecomer and one fears missing the rak'ah, he may gently pull a knowledgeable person who won't be annoyed to stand with him; otherwise he prays alone. This practice refutes the opinion that making space for someone invalidates one's prayer—it does not, as it is a small act and done for Allah and His Messenger. Finally, the author confirms the virtue of front rows, starting with the first, then descending by proximity to the imam, based on the hadith that mercy descends first on the imam and then on those aligned with him.

Key Terms
الصف (al-saff): The row of worshippers in congregational prayer.
الخلل (al-khalal): Gaps between worshippers in a row.
المناكب (al-manakib): Shoulders; aligning them means standing shoulder-to-shoulder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he finds a gap in the first row but the second row is full?
A) He must stay in the second row and not move forward.
B) He may break through the second row to fill the first row gap.
C) He should pray alone behind the rows.
D) He should pull someone from the second row into the first.

Key Takeaway
Row alignment is a sunnah mu'akkadah; one should fill gaps and help others, as it is obedience to the Prophet's command, not ostentation.

Arrangement of Rows in Congregational Prayer
Describes the order of rows with proof and reward details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of rows in congregational prayer, cite the hadith proof, and apply the ruling for khunatha.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice establishes the row order: men, boys, khunatha, women — each in their proper place.

In congregational prayer, the arrangement of worshippers in rows is a confirmed sunnah. This lesson examines the specific order prescribed by the Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet (PBUH). We will also explore the special case of the khuntha mushkil and the multiplication of reward for different positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its evidence
The passage states that the rows are arranged: men nearest the imam, then boys, then khunatha, then women. The proof is a hadith from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari describing the Prophet's action.
The hadith is a fi'l (action) proof, not an explicit command.
2
Analyze the position of boys
Boys come after men. If only one boy is present, he stands among the men, not in a separate row. This shows flexibility when numbers are limited.
The hadith mentions a group of boys; the ruling covers both cases.
3
Explain the ruling for khunatha
Khunatha (ambiguous gender) are placed after boys in a single scattered row. The precaution is to avoid fitna: if they are male, being behind boys is harmless; if female, they are already behind. They are treated with the principle of 'the more harmful possibility'.
They are not made into two rows nor aligned directly due to ambiguity.
4
Discuss the virtue of the first row and reward multiplication
The first row behind the imam carries the greatest reward: 100 prayers. The right side: 75, left side: 50. Other rows: 25 or 5, depending on narration. This encourages competing for the first row.
The multiplication is in addition to the basic 27 or 25 times for congregation.
5
Note the extension to funeral prayers and graves
The same order applies to funeral prayer: men nearest the imam, then boys, etc. In grave placement, men are near the qibla, then others, with dirt barriers if necessary.
This is a practical application of the principle of prioritizing men in proximity to the imam/qibla.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يصف الصبيان لقول أبي مالك الأشعري أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أقام الرجال يلونه، وأقام الصبيان خلف ذلك، وأقام النساء خلف ذلك، وإن لم يكن جمع من الصبيان يقوم الصبي بين الرجال (ثم الخناثي) جمع خنثى والمراد به المشكل احتياطاً لأنه إن كان رجلاً فقيامه خلف الصبيان لا يضره وإن كان امرأة فهو متأخر، ويلزم جعل الخناثي صفاً واحداً متفرقاً اتقاء عن القيام خلف مثله، وعن المحاذاة لاحتمال الذكورة والأنوثة وهو معامل بالأضر في أحواله (ثم) يصف (النساء) إن حضرن وإلا فهن ممنوعات عن حضور الجماعات كما تقدم . من قوله: (ثم إلى الميامن ثم إلى المياسر ) أي من الصف الأول وجمعه باعتبار أن كل واحد القائمين في ميمنة وميسرة قوله (وللذي في سائر الصفوف خمسة وعشرون صلاة) الذي في عبارة غيره خمس بدون تاء هنا وفي الذي قبله وهو الموافق للقواعد النحوية ثم الظاهر أنه بيان لأقل المضاعفة، وإلا فقد تقدّم أنه بكل واحد من الجماعة تزاد صلاة على هذه المضاعفة. قوله : (ثم يصف الصبيان) بكسر الصاد والضم لغة . قوله: القول أبي مالك الخ) لم يذكر الخنائي فيه لندرة وجودهن. قوله: (يقوم الصبي الخ) ولو كان مع رجل تقدمهما الإمام بخلاف المرأة فلا بد من تأخرها. قوله : (ثم الخناث) بالفتح كحبالى ويجمع على خناث كأناس قاموس وهو ماله آلة الرجال، والنساء جميعاً قهستاني أو فاقدهما معاً. قوله : ( لأنه) أي الخنثى المشكل علة لقوله ثم الخناث المقتضى تأخره عن الصبيان. قوله: (وهو معامل بالأضر في أحوال فيقدم على النساء لاحتمال ذكورته، ويؤخر عن الرجال لاحتمال أنوثته، ولا يجعلون صفين لاحتمال أنوثة المتقدم وذكورة المتأخر، ولا يتحاذون لاحتمال الذكورة والأنوثة وتقدم أنه ينويه الإمام وإلا لا تصح صلاته . قوله: (وإلا فهن ممنوعات عن حضور الجماعات مطلقاً ولو كن عجائز قال في زاد الفقير، وعلى هذا الترتيب وضع جنائزهم يعني للصلاة عليهم فيكون الأفضل مما يلي الإمام ومن دونه مما يلي القبلة وفي القبر بالعكس توضع الرجال مما يلي القبلة، ثم سائرهم ويجعل بين كل واحد والآخر حاجز من تراب أو رمل قال شارحه ليصير بمثابة قبرين قال : وهذا عند الضرورة، وإلا فالأفضل وضع كل في قبر على حدة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Then he arranges the boys due to the saying of Abu Malik al-Ash'ari that the Prophet (PBUH) stood the men next to him, stood the boys behind that, and stood the women behind that. And if there is not a group of boys, the boy stands among the men. Then the khunatha (plural of khuntha) meaning the ambiguous [hermaphrodite] as a precaution, because if it is a man, his standing behind the boys does not harm him, and if it is a woman, she is delayed. It is necessary to make the khunatha a single row, separated, to avoid standing behind one like him and to avoid alignment due to the possibility of masculinity and femininity. He is treated according to the more harmful in his states. Then he arranges the women if they are present, otherwise they are prohibited from attending congregations as previously mentioned. From his saying: 'Then to the right side, then to the left side' meaning from the first row, and its plural considering that each of those standing is on the right and left. His saying: 'And for the one in the rest of the rows, twenty-five prayers' which in the wording of others is 'five' without a 'ta' here and in the previous one, and it is in accordance with grammatical rules. Then it appears that it is a statement of the minimum multiplication; otherwise, it was previously mentioned that with each one of the congregation, a prayer is added to this multiplication. His saying: 'Then he arranges the boys' with kasra on the sad, and damm is a language. His saying: 'The saying of Abu Malik etc.' He did not mention the khunatha in it due to their rarity. His saying: 'The boy stands etc.' And if there is a man, the imam precedes them both, unlike the woman, so she must be delayed. His saying: 'Then the khunatha' with fatha like hibala, and it is pluralized as khunath like anas in the Qamus; it is one who has both male and female organs, or lacks both. His saying: 'Because' i.e., the ambiguous khuntha is the reason for his saying 'then the khunatha' necessitating his delay after the boys. His saying: 'He is treated according to the more harmful in his states' so he is placed before women due to the possibility of his masculinity, and delayed after men due to the possibility of his femininity. They are not made into two rows due to the possibility of the femininity of the one in front and masculinity of the one behind, and they do not align due to the possibility of masculinity and femininity. It is previously mentioned that the imam intends him, otherwise his prayer is not valid. His saying: 'Otherwise they are prohibited from attending congregations absolutely, even if they are old women.' He said in Zad al-Faqir: 'And upon this order is the placement of their funerals, meaning for prayer upon them, so the best is that which is near the imam, and what is below is that which is near the qibla. And in the grave, the opposite: men are placed near the qibla, then the rest. And a barrier of dirt or sand is made between each one and the other.' His commentator said: 'So that it becomes like two graves.' He said: 'This is in case of necessity; otherwise, the best is to place each in a separate grave. And Allah the Exalted knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.'
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the arrangement of rows (sufuf) in congregational prayer. The author states that after men, boys are arranged in rows, citing a hadith from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari that the Prophet (PBUH) positioned men nearest to him, then boys behind them, then women behind that. If there is no group of boys, a single boy stands among the men. Then come the khunatha (hermaphrodites), who are placed after boys as a precaution: if they are male, being behind boys is harmless; if female, they are already further back. They must be placed in a single scattered row to avoid standing behind someone of the same ambiguous gender or aligning directly, due to the possibility of masculinity or femininity. The principle of 'treating with the more harmful' (mu'amala bil adarr) applies: they are placed before women (due to possible masculinity) but after men (due to possible femininity). Finally, women are arranged if present; otherwise, they are prohibited from attending congregations. The commentary explains that the reward for the first row is multiplied: for someone standing directly behind the imam, one hundred prayers; on the right, seventy-five; on the left, fifty; and in other rows, twenty-five or five according to some narrations. This shows the virtue of the first row and specific positions. The author then extends the analogy to funeral prayers and graves: the best position for the deceased's body in funeral prayer is near the imam, and in the grave, men are placed near the qibla, with barriers between bodies if necessary.

Key Terms
الخنثى المشكل (al-khuntha al-mushkil): A person whose gender is ambiguous, having both male and female organs or lacking both.
المضاعفة (al-muda'afah): Multiplication of reward for prayer in congregation, especially for specific positions in the row.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should a khuntha mushkil stand in congregational prayer?
A) In the front row with men
B) In a single row behind boys and before women
C) In a separate row behind women
D) Next to the imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of rows in congregational prayer is men, then boys, then khunatha (in a scattered row), then women — based on prophetic practice and precaution against fitna.

Muqtadi Completing Tashahhud After Imam's Salam
Ruling on a follower who has not finished tashahhud when the imam says salam or speaks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on whether a follower must complete tashahhud after the imam's salam, and distinguish the normal case from the case of the imam's intentional hadath.

Core Idea
A follower completes a wajib tashahhud even after the imam's salam, but exits the prayer if the imam intentionally invalidates.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in congregational prayer: the follower is still reciting tashahhud when the imam says salam. According to the Hanafi school, the follower must weigh the obligation of completing the tashahhud against the sunnah of following the imam. Additionally, if the imam intentionally invalidates his prayer, the follower's obligations change entirely. We will examine the positions of the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad, and the conditions that affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
First, distinguish the two main cases in the passage: (1) the imam says salam or speaks normally, and (2) the imam intentionally invalidates the prayer. Each has a different ruling for the follower.
Speech (kalām) is treated like salam, not like hadath.
2
Determine the hukm of tashahhud
Recognize that finishing the tashahhud is a wajib (obligatory) act in the prayer. According to Hanafi fiqh, a wajib must be performed if possible; omitting it without excuse requires compensation (sajdah sahw).
Tashahhud is not a rukn, but its obligation is taken seriously.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf among the Sahibayn and Muhammad
In the normal case, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the follower completes the tashahhud because the sanctity of prayer remains. Imam Muhammad, however, held that the follower exits the prayer with the imam's salam and therefore should not complete it.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn.
4
Apply the rule for intentional hadath
If the imam intentionally invalidates his prayer (e.g., by laughing or speaking deliberately), the follower does not complete the tashahhud nor say salam. The follower's prayer was valid only in connection with the imam's; building on an invalid prayer is not allowed.
If the follower had sat for the duration of tashahhud before the imam's hadath, the follower's prayer remains valid.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi and conditions
Conclude that in the normal case, the follower must complete the tashahhud then say salam. In the hadath case, the follower exits silently and must repeat the prayer (if within the time). The condition for the hadath case is whether the follower had sat for the tashahhud duration.
The ruling is based on the principle: preserving a wajib takes precedence over a sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيما يفعله المقتدي بعد فراغ إمامه من واجب وغيره لو سلم الإمام أو تكلم قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة التشهد يتمه) لأنه من الواجبات، ثم يسلم لبقاء حرمة الصلاة، وأمكن الجمع بالإتيان بهما وإن بقيت الصلوات، والدعوات يتركها، ويسلم مع الإمام لأنّ ترك السنة دون ترك الواجب، وأما إن أحدث الإمام عمداً، ولو بقهقهته عند السلام لا يقرأ المقتدي التشهد ولا يسلم لخروجه من الصلاة ببطلان الجزء الذي لاقاه حدث الإمام فلا يبني على فاسد، ولا يضر في صحة الصلاة لكن يجب إعادتها لجبر نقصها بترك السلام، وإذا لم يجلس قدر التشهد بطلت بالحدث العمد ولو قام الإمام يسجد. قوله : (وغيره) عطف على قوله ما يفعله أي وما لا يفعله كما لو رفع الإمام رأسه قبل تسبيح المقتدي ثلاثاً فإنه لا يتمها ويحتمل غير ذلك. قوله: (أو تكلم) فالكلام منه كالسلام بخلاف الحدث العمد فمفسد قوله : (يتمه) أي على قولهما وقال محمد : لا يتمه لخروجه من الصلاة بسلام إمامه أفاده السيد قوله : (لبقاء حرمة الصلاة) أي في حق المأموم قوله : (وأما إن أحدث الإمام (عمداً احترز بالعمد عما لو سبقه حدث بعد التشهد فإنه يذهب يتوضأ ويسلم ويستخلف من يسلم بالقوم قوله : (فلا يبنى على فاسد) فليس عليه أن يسلم، وإن سلم لا يصادف محلاً قوله : (لكن يجب إعادتها) أي ما دام الوقت
Regarding what the follower does after his imam finishes from an obligatory [act] or other. If the imam says salam or speaks before the follower completes reading the tashahhud, he completes it because it is from the obligatory acts, then he says salam due to the remaining sanctity of the prayer. It is possible to combine both, and even if the blessings and supplications remain, he leaves them and says salam with the imam because leaving a sunnah is less than leaving an obligatory act. And if the imam intentionally invalidates, even by laughter at the time of salam, the follower does not read the tashahhud nor say salam because he exits the prayer by the invalidation of the part that the imam's hadath encountered, so he does not build upon an invalid [prayer]. It does not harm the validity of the prayer, but it must be repeated to compensate for its deficiency by leaving the salam. And if he did not sit for the duration of the tashahhud, it is invalidated by intentional hadath, even if the imam stood to prostrate. His saying: 'and other' is a conjunction to his saying 'what he does' meaning what he does not do, like if the imam raises his head before the follower's tasbih three times, then he does not complete it, and other possibilities. His saying: 'or speaks' so speech from him is like salam unlike intentional hadath which invalidates. His saying: 'he completes it' i.e., according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Muhammad said: he does not complete it because he exits the prayer by the salam of his imam. This was benefited by al-Sayyid. His saying: 'due to the remaining sanctity of the prayer' i.e., with respect to the follower. His saying: 'And if the imam intentionally invalidates' he restricts with 'intentional' as opposed to if an event precedes after tashahhud: then he goes to perform wudu and says salam and appoints someone to say salam with the people. His saying: 'so he does not build upon an invalid [prayer]' so he is not obliged to say salam, and if he says salam, it does not encounter a valid place. His saying: 'but it must be repeated' i.e., as long as the time remains.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a follower who has not completed the tashahhud when the imam says salam or speaks. The relied-upon position (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, i.e., the Sahibayn) is that the follower should complete the obligatory tashahhud first, then say salam, because the sanctity of the prayer remains for him. He leaves the optional blessings and supplications to follow the imam in salam, as preserving an obligatory act (the tashahhud) takes precedence over a sunnah (salam with imam immediately). However, Imam Muhammad holds that the follower does not complete the tashahhud because he exits the prayer with the imam's salam. The text then discusses a scenario where the imam intentionally invalidates the prayer (e.g., by laughing at the time of salam). In that case, the follower should not complete tashahhud nor say salam, because the imam's prayer is invalidated, and the follower's prayer was valid only in connection with the imam's prayer; building on an invalid prayer is not allowed. The follower's prayer is valid but must be repeated due to missing the salam. If the imam's hadath occurs after the follower has sat for the duration of tashahhud, the follower may complete the prayer. The authority weight here is from the commentary of al-Tahtawi, which is a later source (fatawa mutakhkhirin), but the ruling is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah positions of the Sahibayn and Muhammad.

Key Terms
حرمة الصلاة (hurmat al-salah): The inviolability and legal continuity of the prayer; once in prayer, certain actions become forbidden.
يتمه (yutimmuhu): He completes it (the tashahhud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, what should a follower do if the imam says salam while the follower is still in tashahhud?
A) Immediately say salam
B) Complete the tashahhud then say salam
C) Repeat the prayer
D) Make sujud al-sahw

Key Takeaway
The follower must complete the wajib tashahhud before saying salam, unless the imam's prayer is invalidated by intentional hadath – then the follower exits silently and repeats the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Three Types of Followers: Mudrik, Lahiqa, Masbuq
Defines three follower types and their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of followers in congregational prayer and state the rulings for makeup rak'ahs of the lahiq and masbuq.

Core Idea
The lahiqa does not recite in missed rak'ahs; the masbuq recites in first two makeup rak'ahs and sits for tashahhud.

In congregational prayer, not all followers complete every rak'ah with the imam. Some join late or miss parts due to valid excuses. The Hanafi tradition classifies followers into three types: mudrik (full follower), lahiq (missed due to excuse), and masbuq (latecomer). Each has distinct rulings for making up missed parts. This lesson unpacks these categories and their specific rules, including a subtle disagreement within the school about the order of makeup.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
From the passage, list the three types of followers: mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq. Note the defining characteristic of each: mudrik completes all rak'ahs with the imam; lahiq entered with the imam but missed some due to a valid excuse (sleep, forgetfulness, etc.); masbuq joined after the imam had already started.
The mudrik requires no special rulings; focus on lahiq and masbuq.
2
Understand the lahiq's rulings
The lahiq is considered a true follower (mu'tam) for the missed parts. He does not recite Qur'an or tashahhud in his makeup rak'ahs, nor does he perform sahw prostration for his own errors. His obligation remains as originally intended (e.g., if he intended residency behind a traveller imam, his prayer does not become four rak'ahs). He must make up missed rak'ahs after the imam finishes, then follow the imam for the rest if possible.
The lahiq's makeup is silent; he is still attached to the imam's congregation.
3
Analyze the masbuq's rulings
The masbuq makes up rak'ahs independently. He recites in the first two rak'ahs of his makeup (if his makeup includes two or more) and sits for tashahhud at the end of his makeup. He is independent except in four specific cases. He also recites takbirat al-tashriq by consensus. If the imam performs sahw prostration, the masbuq follows if he has not yet tied the rak'ah with a prostration.
The masbuq's makeup mirrors an individual prayer for recitation and sitting.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on order
The passage mentions that if the lahiq (who is also masbuq) reverses the order of his makeup (e.g., prays with recitation before without), the prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa but sinful, while Zufar holds it invalid. This shows the school's internal flexibility and the emphasis on proper sequence.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa: valid but sinful.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a person who joins the Isha prayer after two rak'ahs (masbuq). He must make up two rak'ahs with recitation, then sit for tashahhud. If a person falls asleep and misses a rak'ah (lahiq), he makes up that rak'ah without recitation after the imam finishes.
Practice distinguishing the two scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن المقتدي ثلاثة أقسام مدرك ولاحق ومسبوق فالمدرك من صلى الركعات كلها مع الإمام، واللاحق هو من دخل معه وفاته كلها أو بعضها بأن عرض له نوم أو غفلة، أو زحمة أو سبق حدث، أو كان مقيماً خلف مسافر، وحكمه كمؤتم حقيقة فلا يأتي فيما يقضي بقراءة ولا سهو ولا يتغير فرضه أربعاً بنية الإقامة، ويبدأ بقضاء ما فاته، ثم يتبع إمامه إن أمكنه أن يدركه بعد ذلك فيسلم معه، وإلا تابعه ولا يشتغل بالقضاء حتى يفرغ الإمام من صلاته ولا مع الإمام لسهو الإمام، بل يقوم للقضاء ثم يسجد عن ذلك بعد الختم، ولا يقعد عن الثانية إذا لم يقعد الإمام، ولا يقتدي به فإن كان مسبوقاً أيضاً فقام للقضاء فإنه يصلي أولاً ما نام فيه مثلاً بلا قراءة، ثم يصلي ما سبق به بها، ولو عکس صح عندنا خلافاً لزفر وأثم لترك الترتيب كما في الفتح، وغيره والمسبوق هو من سبقه الإمام بكلها أو بعضها وحكمه أنه يقضي أول صلاته في حق القراءة وآخرها في حق القعدة وهو منفرد فيما يقضيه إلا في أربع لا يجوز اقتداؤه، ولا الاقتداء به ويأتي بتكبيرات التشريق إجماعاً ولو كبر ينوي الاستئناف للصلاة مستأنفاً ولو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وسجد أمامه لسهو تابعه فيه إن لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة فإن لم يتابعه سجد في آخر صلاته.
Know that the follower is of three types: mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq. The mudrik is one who prayed all the rak'ahs with the imam. The lahiq is one who entered with him but missed all or some [rak'ahs] due to sleep, absentmindedness, crowding, a preceding hadath, or being a resident behind a traveller. His ruling is like a true follower: he does not recite in what he makes up, nor sahw, and his obligation does not change to four by intention of residency. He begins by making up what he missed, then follows his imam if he can catch him later and then says salam with him; otherwise, he follows him and does not occupy himself with making up until the imam finishes his prayer, nor with the imam due to the imam's sahw. Rather, he stands for making up and then prostrates for that after completion. He does not sit for the second [tashahhud] if the imam did not sit, nor does he follow [the imam] in that. If he is also masbuq and stood for making up, he first prays what he slept in, for example, without recitation, then prays what he was preceded in with recitation. If he reverses, it is valid according to us, contrary to Zufar, but he sins for abandoning the order, as in al-Fath and others. The masbuq is one whom the imam preceded in all or some [rak'ahs]. His ruling is that he makes up the first of his prayer with respect to recitation and the last with respect to sitting, and he is independent in what he makes up, except in four [cases]: it is not permissible for him to follow [another], nor for another to follow him. He says the takbirat al-tashriq by consensus. If he says takbir intending to restart the prayer anew, and if he stood to make up what he was preceded in and the imam prostrated for sahw, he follows him in that if he did not tie the rak'ah with a prostration; if he did not follow him, he prostrates at the end of his prayer.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the three categories of followers (muqtadi) in congregational prayer. The mudrik is one who performed all rak'ahs with the imam; no special rulings apply to him beyond normal. The lahiq is one who entered with the imam but missed some rak'ahs due to valid reasons like sleep, forgetfulness, or being a resident following a traveller imam. The lahiq's ruling is similar to a true follower (mu'tam) in that he does not recite (Qur'an or tashahhud) in the rak'ahs he makes up, nor does he perform sahw prostration for his own errors, and his obligation is not changed to four if he intends residency while behind a traveller. He must first make up the missed rak'ahs after the imam finishes, then follow the imam for the remaining parts if possible. If he is also a masbuq (i.e., he missed part and then also lagged behind), he prays first the missed part without recitation, then the part he missed with recitation. Reversing the order is valid but sinful (according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Zufar). The masbuq is one who joined late and missed some rak'ahs. His ruling is that he makes up the first part of his prayer regarding recitation (i.e., he recites in the first two rak'ahs of his makeup) and the last part regarding sitting (i.e., he sits for tashahhud at the end of his makeup). He is independent in his makeup except in four situations where following is not allowed. He also says the takbirat al-tashriq by consensus. If the imam makes sahw prostration, the masbuq should follow if he has not yet tied the rak'ah with a sajdah (i.e., if he is still in that rak'ah). This passage is a parsing exercise that defines key terms and summarizes the complex rulings on latecomers.

Key Terms
المدرك (al-mudrik): A follower who performs all rak'ahs with the imam from beginning to end.
اللاحق (al-lahiqa): A follower who entered prayer with the imam but missed part due to a valid excuse.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A follower who joined late and missed one or more rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of follower does not recite Qur'an in the rak'ahs they make up?
A) Mudrik
B) Lahiqa
C) Masbuq
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The lahiqa makes up missed rak'ahs without recitation; the masbuq recites in the first two makeup rak'ahs and sits for tashahhud at the end.

Completing Tashahhud After Imam's Salam
Ruling on follower completing tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a follower must complete the wajib tashahhud before saying salam, even if the imam concludes first, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue.

Core Idea
Complete wajib first: follower finishes tashahhud even if imam says salam.

This passage addresses a common scenario: the imam says salam or speaks before the follower finishes reciting tashahhud. The Hanafi school prioritizes fulfilling the wajib over immediate following. The follower must complete the tashahhud, then say salam, leaving extra du'as. This lesson explains the reasoning and the difference among the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (follower completing tashahhud after imam's salam) and its hukm level (wajib).
2
Locate the proof
The text argues based on the principle that wajib takes precedence over sunnah, and the remaining sanctity of prayer (baqa' hurmat al-salat). No explicit Quran/hadith is cited; the proof is talil (rational reasoning).
The proof is implicit: leaving wajib harms the prayer more than delaying the follow.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative to complete tashahhud arises from its wajib status. The follower's prayer remains valid until salam, so a wajib must be fulfilled before exiting.
The phrase 'li annahu min al-wajibat' directly links the ruling to the category of wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that the follower's prayer ends with the imam's salam, so no completion is needed.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: complete tashahhud. This is because abandoning a wajib is not permissible when a remedy (completing then salam) is available.
Al-Tahtawi confirms the mufta bihi is to complete tashahhud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي بعد فراغ إمامه من واجب وغيره لو سلم الإمام أو تكلم قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة التشهد يتمه لأنه من الواجبات، ثم يسلم لبقاء حرمة الصلاة، وأمكن الجمع بالإتيان بهما وإن بقيت الصلوات، والدعوات يتركها، ويسلم مع الإمام لأن ترك السنة دون ترك الواجب، وأما إن أحدث الإمام عمداً، ولو بقهقهته عند السلام لا يقرأ المقتدي التشهد ولا يسلم لخروجه من الصلاة ببطلان الجزء الذي لاقاه حدث الإمام فلا يبني على فاسد، ولا يضر في صحة الصلاة لكن يجب إعادتها لجبر نقصها بترك السلام، وإذا لم يجلس قدر التشهد بطلت بالحدث العمد ولو قام الإمام يسجد فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي اعلم أن المقتدي ثلاثة أقسام مدرك ولاحق ومسبوق فالمدرك من صلى الركعات كلها مع الإمام، واللاحق هو من دخل معه وفاته كلها أو بعضها بأن عرض له نوم أو غفلة، أو زحمة أو سبق حدث، أو كان مقيماً خلف مسافر، وحكمه كمؤتم حقيقة فلا يأتي فيما يقضي بقراءة ولا سهو ولا يتغير فرضه أربعاً بنية الإقامة، ويبدأ بقضاء ما فاته، ثم يتبع إمامه إن أمكنه أن يدركه بعد ذلك فيسلم معه، وإلا تابعه ولا يشتغل بالقضاء حتى يفرغ الإمام من صلاته ولا مع الإمام لسهو الإمام، بل يقوم للقضاء ثم يسجد عن ذلك بعد الختم، ولا يقعد عن الثانية إذا لم يقعد الإمام، ولا يقتدي به فإن كان مسبوقاً أيضاً فقام للقضاء فإنه يصلي أولاً ما نام فيه مثلاً بلا قراءة، ثم يصلي ما سبق به بها، ولو عكس صح عندنا خلافاً لزفر وأثم لترك الترتيب كما في الفتح، وغيره والمسبوق هو من سبقه الإمام بكلها أو بعضها وحكمه أنه يقضي أول صلاته في حق القراءة وآخرها في حق القعدة وهو منفرد فيما يقضيه إلا في أربع لا يجوز اقتداؤه، ولا الاقتداء به ويأتي بتكبيرات التشريق إجماعاً ولو كبر ينوي الاستئناف للصلاة مستأنفاً ولو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وسجد أمامه لسهو تابعه فيه إن لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة فإن لم يتابعه سجد في آخر صلاته.
Section on what the follower does after his imam finishes from obligatory and other. If the imam says salam or speaks before the follower completes recitation of tashahhud, he completes it because it is from the obligations, then says salam due to the remaining sanctity of the prayer, and it is possible to combine both by doing them, even if the prayers and supplications remain, he leaves them and says salam with the imam because leaving the sunnah is less than leaving the obligation. As for if the imam intentionally breaks wudu, even by laughing out loud during salam, the follower does not recite tashahhud nor say salam because he exits from prayer by the invalidation of the part that the imam's hadath encountered, so he does not build on a corrupted [prayer]. It does not harm the validity of the prayer, but it must be repeated to compensate its deficiency due to leaving salam. And if he did not sit for the duration of tashahhud, it is invalidated by intentional hadath, even if the imam stands to prostrate. Chapter on what the follower does: Know that the follower is of three types: mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq. The mudrik is the one who prayed all the rak'ahs with the imam. The lahiq is the one who entered with him but missed all or some because of sleep, heedlessness, crowding, earlier hadath, or being a resident behind a traveler. His ruling is like a true follower; so in what he makes up he does not recite nor have forgetfulness prostration, and his obligatory number does not change to four by intention of residency. He begins by making up what he missed, then follows his imam if possible after that, and says salam with him. Otherwise, he follows and does not occupy himself with making up until the imam finishes his prayer; nor with the imam concerning the imam's forgetfulness, rather he stands for the makeup then prostrates for that after completion. He does not sit for the second if the imam did not sit, and he does not follow him. If he is also masbuq and stands for makeup, he first prays what he slept in, for example, without recitation, then he prays what he was preceded in with recitation. Even if he reverses, it is valid according to us, contrary to Zufar, but he sins for abandoning order as in al-Fath and others. The masbuq is the one the imam preceded him in all or some of the prayer. His ruling is that he prays the first part of his prayer regarding recitation and the last regarding sitting, and he is alone in what he makes up except in four: his following is not valid, nor is it valid to follow him. He performs the takbirat al-tashriq by consensus. Even if he makes takbir intending to restart the prayer as a fresh start; even if he stands to make up what he was preceded in and his imam prostrated for forgetfulness, he follows him in it if he did not tie the rak'ah with a prostration; if he did not follow him, he prostrates at the end of his prayer.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a ruling section from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, detailing the actions of a follower (muqtadi) after the imam concludes his prayer. The first part addresses the situation when the imam says salam or speaks before the follower finishes reciting the tashahhud. The follower must complete the tashahhud because it is wajib (obligatory), then say salam. He should leave other supererogatory supplications (which are sunnah) to follow the imam, since leaving a sunnah is less harmful than leaving a wajib. If the imam intentionally nullifies his wudu (e.g., by laughing out loud) after the final sitting, the follower should not recite tashahhud or say salam, because the imam's prayer is invalid and the follower cannot build on a corrupted prayer. The follower's own prayer is still valid, but must be repeated later. The text then introduces the three categories of followers: mudrik (one who joins from the beginning and completes with the imam), lahiq (one who misses some part due to sleep, crowding, etc., but remains in the same intention), and masbuq (one who arrives late). For the lahiq, when making up missed rak'ahs, he does not recite or perform sajda sahw, and his prayer remains as he initially intended (e.g., not changing to four if he intended two as a resident behind a traveler). He prioritizes making up missed parts after the imam's salam. For the masbuq, when making up, he recites in the first rak'ahs of his own prayer (which correspond to the imam's later rak'ahs) and sits in the last. He is considered alone in his makeup for recitation and prostration, but must follow the imam in takbirat al-tashriq by consensus. The passage follows the Hanafi school's reliance on balancing wajib and sunnah, and clarifies the distinctions between follower types.

Key Terms
مقتدي (muqtadi): A person who prays behind an imam, i.e., a follower in congregational prayer.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element of prayer that, if left intentionally, invalidates the prayer; if left forgetfully, requires sajda sahw.
التشهد (tashahhud): The recitation of at-tahiyyat and related supplications in the final sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should a follower do if the imam says salam before the follower finishes reciting tashahhud?
A) Stop reciting and say salam with the imam immediately.
B) Complete the tashahhud, then say salam.
C) Leave tashahhud and not say salam, since the imam ended prayer.
D) Recite tashahhud but not say salam, and wait for imam.

Key Takeaway
A follower must complete the wajib tashahhud before saying salam, even if the imam finishes first, because preserving the wajib takes precedence over immediate following.

Follower's Action When Imam Intentionally Nullifies Wudu
Ruling on follower when imam intentionally breaks wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a follower when the imam intentionally invalidates his wudu during prayers, and explain why the follower does not complete tashahhud or salam.

Core Idea
Imam's intentional hadath invalidates his prayer; follower cannot build on corrupted prayer.

The text presents a second scenario: the imam intentionally breaks his wudu (even by laughing out loud) at the time of salam. In this case, the follower does not complete tashahhud or say salam, because the imam's prayer becomes invalid and the follower cannot rely on a nullified prayer. However, the follower's own prayer remains valid, though it must be repeated later to compensate for leaving the salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam intentionally breaks wudu (hadath 'amd) after the final sitting, e.g., by laughing loudly during salam.
This is different from unintentional hadath, which has different rulings.
2
Determine the effect on imam's prayer
The imam's prayer becomes invalid (batil) because his part that encountered hadath is nullified.
3
Determine the follower's obligation
The follower does NOT recite tashahhud nor say salam, because he cannot build his prayer on a corrupted base (la yabni 'ala fásid).
The follower's prayer is still valid given he was following a valid imam initially, but the ending is affected.
4
Understand the consequence for follower's prayer
The follower's prayer is valid (la yadurr fi sihha al-salat), but it must be repeated (tu'adu) to compensate for the missing salam.
If the follower did not sit for the duration of tashahhud, intentional hadath invalidates his prayer completely.
5
Note the exception condition
If the follower had not sat for the duration of tashahhud before the imam's hadath, then the follower's prayer is also invalidated by the intentional hadath.
This shows that if the follower's own prayer was already incomplete in its obligatory sitting, the imam's hadath nullifies it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي بعد فراغ إمامه من واجب وغيره لو سلم الإمام أو تكلم قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة التشهد يتمه لأنه من الواجبات، ثم يسلم لبقاء حرمة الصلاة، وأمكن الجمع بالإتيان بهما وإن بقيت الصلوات، والدعوات يتركها، ويسلم مع الإمام لأن ترك السنة دون ترك الواجب، وأما إن أحدث الإمام عمداً، ولو بقهقهته عند السلام لا يقرأ المقتدي التشهد ولا يسلم لخروجه من الصلاة ببطلان الجزء الذي لاقاه حدث الإمام فلا يبني على فاسد، ولا يضر في صحة الصلاة لكن يجب إعادتها لجبر نقصها بترك السلام، وإذا لم يجلس قدر التشهد بطلت بالحدث العمد ولو قام الإمام يسجد فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي اعلم أن المقتدي ثلاثة أقسام مدرك ولاحق ومسبوق فالمدرك من صلى الركعات كلها مع الإمام، واللاحق هو من دخل معه وفاته كلها أو بعضها بأن عرض له نوم أو غفلة، أو زحمة أو سبق حدث، أو كان مقيماً خلف مسافر، وحكمه كمؤتم حقيقة فلا يأتي فيما يقضي بقراءة ولا سهو ولا يتغير فرضه أربعاً بنية الإقامة، ويبدأ بقضاء ما فاته، ثم يتبع إمامه إن أمكنه أن يدركه بعد ذلك فيسلم معه، وإلا تابعه ولا يشتغل بالقضاء حتى يفرغ الإمام من صلاته ولا مع الإمام لسهو الإمام، بل يقوم للقضاء ثم يسجد عن ذلك بعد الختم، ولا يقعد عن الثانية إذا لم يقعد الإمام، ولا يقتدي به فإن كان مسبوقاً أيضاً فقام للقضاء فإنه يصلي أولاً ما نام فيه مثلاً بلا قراءة، ثم يصلي ما سبق به بها، ولو عكس صح عندنا خلافاً لزفر وأثم لترك الترتيب كما في الفتح، وغيره والمسبوق هو من سبقه الإمام بكلها أو بعضها وحكمه أنه يقضي أول صلاته في حق القراءة وآخرها في حق القعدة وهو منفرد فيما يقضيه إلا في أربع لا يجوز اقتداؤه، ولا الاقتداء به ويأتي بتكبيرات التشريق إجماعاً ولو كبر ينوي الاستئناف للصلاة مستأنفاً ولو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وسجد أمامه لسهو تابعه فيه إن لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة فإن لم يتابعه سجد في آخر صلاته.
Section on what the follower does after his imam finishes from obligatory and other. If the imam says salam or speaks before the follower completes recitation of tashahhud, he completes it because it is from the obligations, then says salam due to the remaining sanctity of the prayer, and it is possible to combine both by doing them, even if the prayers and supplications remain, he leaves them and says salam with the imam because leaving the sunnah is less than leaving the obligation. As for if the imam intentionally breaks wudu, even by laughing out loud during salam, the follower does not recite tashahhud nor say salam because he exits from prayer by the invalidation of the part that the imam's hadath encountered, so he does not build on a corrupted [prayer]. It does not harm the validity of the prayer, but it must be repeated to compensate its deficiency due to leaving salam. And if he did not sit for the duration of tashahhud, it is invalidated by intentional hadath, even if the imam stands to prostrate. Chapter on what the follower does: Know that the follower is of three types: mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq. The mudrik is the one who prayed all the rak'ahs with the imam. The lahiq is the one who entered with him but missed all or some because of sleep, heedlessness, crowding, earlier hadath, or being a resident behind a traveler. His ruling is like a true follower; so in what he makes up he does not recite nor have forgetfulness prostration, and his obligatory number does not change to four by intention of residency. He begins by making up what he missed, then follows his imam if possible after that, and says salam with him. Otherwise, he follows and does not occupy himself with making up until the imam finishes his prayer; nor with the imam concerning the imam's forgetfulness, rather he stands for the makeup then prostrates for that after completion. He does not sit for the second if the imam did not sit, and he does not follow him. If he is also masbuq and stands for makeup, he first prays what he slept in, for example, without recitation, then he prays what he was preceded in with recitation. Even if he reverses, it is valid according to us, contrary to Zufar, but he sins for abandoning order as in al-Fath and others. The masbuq is the one the imam preceded him in all or some of the prayer. His ruling is that he prays the first part of his prayer regarding recitation and the last regarding sitting, and he is alone in what he makes up except in four: his following is not valid, nor is it valid to follow him. He performs the takbirat al-tashriq by consensus. Even if he makes takbir intending to restart the prayer as a fresh start; even if he stands to make up what he was preceded in and his imam prostrated for forgetfulness, he follows him in it if he did not tie the rak'ah with a prostration; if he did not follow him, he prostrates at the end of his prayer.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a ruling section from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, detailing the actions of a follower (muqtadi) after the imam concludes his prayer. The first part addresses the situation when the imam says salam or speaks before the follower finishes reciting the tashahhud. The follower must complete the tashahhud because it is wajib (obligatory), then say salam. He should leave other supererogatory supplications (which are sunnah) to follow the imam, since leaving a sunnah is less harmful than leaving a wajib. If the imam intentionally nullifies his wudu (e.g., by laughing out loud) after the final sitting, the follower should not recite tashahhud or say salam, because the imam's prayer is invalid and the follower cannot build on a corrupted prayer. The follower's own prayer is still valid, but must be repeated later. The text then introduces the three categories of followers: mudrik (one who joins from the beginning and completes with the imam), lahiq (one who misses some part due to sleep, crowding, etc., but remains in the same intention), and masbuq (one who arrives late). For the lahiq, when making up missed rak'ahs, he does not recite or perform sajda sahw, and his prayer remains as he initially intended (e.g., not changing to four if he intended two as a resident behind a traveler). He prioritizes making up missed parts after the imam's salam. For the masbuq, when making up, he recites in the first rak'ahs of his own prayer (which correspond to the imam's later rak'ahs) and sits in the last. He is considered alone in his makeup for recitation and prostration, but must follow the imam in takbirat al-tashriq by consensus. The passage follows the Hanafi school's reliance on balancing wajib and sunnah, and clarifies the distinctions between follower types.

Key Terms
حدث عمد (hadath 'amd): Intentional breaking of wudu, e.g., by laughing out loud, speaking, etc.
إعادة (i'ada): Repeating the prayer; in this context, wajib to compensate for missing salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam intentionally breaks wudu during the final salam, and the follower had already sat for the duration of tashahhud, what is the status of the follower's prayer?
A) It is invalid (batil) and must be repeated.
B) It is valid and does not need to be repeated.
C) It is valid but must be repeated (wajib).
D) It is valid and the follower may leave without salam.

Key Takeaway
When the imam intentionally invalidates wudu, the follower does not complete tashahhud or salam; his prayer is valid but must be repeated to compensate for the missing salam.
