Categories of Followers: Mudrik, Lahiq, and Masbuq
Classification of followers and their makeup rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of followers in Hanafi fiqh (mudrik, lahiq, masbuq) and state the specific rulings for the lahiq and masbuq regarding recitation, forgetfulness prostration, and order of makeup.

Core Idea
Three follower types: mudrik (complete), lahiq (missed part due to excuse), masbuq (joined late) – each has distinct makeup rules.

This passage classifies followers into three categories: mudrik (one who prays all rak'ahs with the imam), lahiq (one who entered with the imam but missed some parts due to sleep, crowding, etc.), and masbuq (one who joins late, missing one or more rak'ahs). The rulings for lahiq and masbuq in making up missed parts differ significantly: the lahiq does not recite or prostrate for forgetfulness in his makeup, while the masbuq recites in the first part of his makeup and sits at the end. The text also addresses the order of makeup for a combined lahiq-masbuq and a disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Define the three categories
Identify mudrik (completed with imam), lahiq (missed due to excuse, still in intention), and masbuq (joined late).
The lahiq is unique to Hanafi; he remains a true follower in essence.
2
Understand the lahiq's makeup ruling
In making up missed rak'ahs, the lahiq does NOT recite (no qira'at) and does NOT perform sajda sahw, and his obligatory number does not change (e.g., if he intended 4, he must still make up 4).
He makes up what he missed exactly as if he were still following the imam in that part.
3
Understand the masbuq's makeup ruling
In making up, the masbuq prays the first part of his own prayer regarding recitation (i.e., he recites in the first rak'ahs he makes up) and the last part regarding sitting (i.e., he sits for tashahhud at the end). He is alone in his makeup for recitation and sajda sahw.
The masbuq must follow the imam in takbirat al-tashriq by consensus.
4
Analyze the order of makeup for lahiq-masbuq
If a follower is both lahiq and masbuq (e.g., he missed some rak'ahs due to sleep and also joined late), he first makes up the missed rak'ahs due to the excuse (without recitation), then makes up those he missed due to late arrival (with recitation). Reversing the order is valid but sinful.
This is the Hanafi position; Zufar disagrees and holds reversal invalid.
5
Note exceptional cases for masbuq
The masbuq is considered alone in his makeup except in four specific matters (not detailed here). His following of the imam in sajda sahw is conditional: if he has not tied the rak'ah with a prostration, he follows; otherwise, he prostrates at the end of his own prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي بعد فراغ إمامه من واجب وغيره لو سلم الإمام أو تكلم قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة التشهد يتمه لأنه من الواجبات، ثم يسلم لبقاء حرمة الصلاة، وأمكن الجمع بالإتيان بهما وإن بقيت الصلوات، والدعوات يتركها، ويسلم مع الإمام لأن ترك السنة دون ترك الواجب، وأما إن أحدث الإمام عمداً، ولو بقهقهته عند السلام لا يقرأ المقتدي التشهد ولا يسلم لخروجه من الصلاة ببطلان الجزء الذي لاقاه حدث الإمام فلا يبني على فاسد، ولا يضر في صحة الصلاة لكن يجب إعادتها لجبر نقصها بترك السلام، وإذا لم يجلس قدر التشهد بطلت بالحدث العمد ولو قام الإمام يسجد فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي اعلم أن المقتدي ثلاثة أقسام مدرك ولاحق ومسبوق فالمدرك من صلى الركعات كلها مع الإمام، واللاحق هو من دخل معه وفاته كلها أو بعضها بأن عرض له نوم أو غفلة، أو زحمة أو سبق حدث، أو كان مقيماً خلف مسافر، وحكمه كمؤتم حقيقة فلا يأتي فيما يقضي بقراءة ولا سهو ولا يتغير فرضه أربعاً بنية الإقامة، ويبدأ بقضاء ما فاته، ثم يتبع إمامه إن أمكنه أن يدركه بعد ذلك فيسلم معه، وإلا تابعه ولا يشتغل بالقضاء حتى يفرغ الإمام من صلاته ولا مع الإمام لسهو الإمام، بل يقوم للقضاء ثم يسجد عن ذلك بعد الختم، ولا يقعد عن الثانية إذا لم يقعد الإمام، ولا يقتدي به فإن كان مسبوقاً أيضاً فقام للقضاء فإنه يصلي أولاً ما نام فيه مثلاً بلا قراءة، ثم يصلي ما سبق به بها، ولو عكس صح عندنا خلافاً لزفر وأثم لترك الترتيب كما في الفتح، وغيره والمسبوق هو من سبقه الإمام بكلها أو بعضها وحكمه أنه يقضي أول صلاته في حق القراءة وآخرها في حق القعدة وهو منفرد فيما يقضيه إلا في أربع لا يجوز اقتداؤه، ولا الاقتداء به ويأتي بتكبيرات التشريق إجماعاً ولو كبر ينوي الاستئناف للصلاة مستأنفاً ولو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وسجد أمامه لسهو تابعه فيه إن لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة فإن لم يتابعه سجد في آخر صلاته.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): A follower who completes all rak'ahs with the imam from the beginning.
لاحق (lahiq): A follower who started with the imam but missed some rak'ahs due to an excuse (sleep, forgetfulness, etc.) and remains in the same intention; he makes up without recitation.
مسبوق (masbuq): A follower who joins the congregation late, missing one or more rak'ahs; he makes up with recitation and sits at the end.

Follower's Salam Before Imam: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling on follower's early salam with proof and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a follower reciting salam before the imam, explain the evidence, and identify when it becomes permissible due to necessity.

Core Idea
The follower's salam before the imam is makruh tahrimi but valid; exceptions exist for valid excuses.

In congregational prayer, the follower must follow the imam in all actions, including the final salutation. What happens if the follower says salam before the imam? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, the prohibition's basis, and the exceptional cases where it is allowed to preserve the prayer's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower reciting salam after his tashahhud but before the imam's salam. The text rules it as 'makruh' and the commentary specifies it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The ruling applies to the follower's prayer, not the imam's.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The prohibition is based on the principle of al-mutaba'ah (following the imam) and the hadith prohibition of differing from the imam. The commentator explicitly mentions 'an al-ikhtilaf 'ala al-imam.'
The dalil is a general principle from Sunnah ahad, making it zanni al-thubut.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a dispute about the imam's prayer validity if the follower's early salam was caused by the imam. The weaker view holds the imam's prayer invalid; the correct (sahih) view holds it valid.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the follower's ruling.
4
Apply the exceptions
The text lists valid excuses (e.g., fear of breaking wind, missing Fajr time) when the early salam is not disliked. In such cases, the follower may stand after sitting for the tashahhud and salam before the imam.
These exceptions preserve the prayer from corruption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القعود الأخير في محله وكره) سلام المقتدي بعد تشهد الإمام لوجود فرض القعود (قبل سلامه لتركه المتابعة، وصحت صلاته حتى لا تبطل بطلوع الشمس في الفجر، ووجدان الماء للمتيمم، وبطلت صلاة الإمام على المرجوح وعلى الصحيح صحت كما سنذكره . قوله: (وكره سلام المقتدي الخ) أي تحريماً للنهي عن الاختلاف على الإمام(۱) إلا أن يكون القيام لضرورة صون صلاته عن الفساد كخوف حدث لو انتظر السلام وخروج وقت فجر وجمعة وعيد ومعذور، وتمام مدة مسح ومرور ماز بين ،یدیه فلا يكره حينئذ أن يقوم بعد القعود قدر التشهد قبل السلام قوله : ( لوجود فرض القعود الأولى تأخيره بعد قوله، وصحت صلاته قوله : (التركه المتابعة) علة لقوله وكره وأفاد به أن الكراهة تحريمية. قوله : (وبطلت صلاة الإمام أي بوجود ما ذكر قوله : ( على المرجوح) وهو القول بأن الخروج بالصنع فرض قوله : (وعلى الصحيح أي من عدم افتراض الخروج بالصنع قوله: (كما سنذكره) أي في المسائل الأثنى عشرية إن شاء الله تعالى والله عز وجل أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
(۱) قوله إلا أن يكون القيام الخ مقتضى هذه العبارة أن لفظ المصنف وكره قيام المقتدي الخ لإسلام المقتدي فليتأمل ويحرر اهـ مصححه .
The last sitting is in its place, and it is disliked (for the follower to recite) the salam after the imam's tashahhud due to the obligation of sitting (before the imam's salam), (and it is disliked) because he abandons following (the imam). And his prayer is valid, such that it is not invalidated by sunrise during Fajr or by finding water for one who performed tayammum. And the imam's prayer is invalid according to the less preponderant view, while according to the correct view it is valid, as we will mention. He said: (And it is disliked for the follower to recite salam, etc.) meaning it is prohibitively disliked due to the prohibition of differing from the imam, unless he stands out of necessity to preserve his prayer from corruption, such as fear of breaking wind if he waits for the salam, or the departure of the time for Fajr, Jumu'ah, 'Eid, or an excuse, or the completion of the period for wiping, or the passing of something in front of him. In such cases, it is not disliked for him to stand after sitting for the duration of the tashahhud before the salam. He said: (Due to the obligation of sitting) — it is better to delay (the salam) after his saying, and his prayer is valid. He said: (Abandoning following) is the reason for his saying 'it is disliked', and he indicated that the dislike is prohibitively so. He said: (And the imam's prayer is invalid) meaning due to the occurrence of what was mentioned. He said: (According to the less preponderant view) is the view that exiting the prayer by action is obligatory. He said: (And according to the correct view) is the lack of obligation of exiting by action. He said: (As we will mention) meaning in the twelve issues, God willing. And Allah Almighty knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Footnote: His saying 'unless he stands' etc. The implication of this expression is that the author's wording is 'and it is disliked for the follower to stand' for the salam of the follower. So let it be pondered and corrected. End. Corrected by the proofreader.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific ruling regarding the follower (muqtadi) in congregational prayer. The author states that it is makruh for the follower to recite the salam (taslim) before the imam, even after completing his own tashahhud, because he abandons the obligation of following the imam (mutaba'ah). However, the follower's prayer remains valid; it is not nullified by external factors like sunrise during Fajr prayer or the follower who performed tayammum finding water after the prayer. The imam's prayer, according to a weaker view, is invalidated if he causes such a situation, but the correct view (sahih) is that it remains valid. The commentary then explains that the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) due to the prohibition of differing from the imam, citing the hadith principle that the imam is followed. However, there are exceptions: if the follower has a valid excuse (such as fear of breaking wind, missing the Fajr time, Jumu'ah, 'Eid, or having something pass in front of him), then it is not disliked for him to stand after sitting for the tashahhud and to say salam before the imam. The commentator also clarifies that the word 'sitting' (al-qu'ud) here refers to the final sitting, and the obligation (fard) of sitting is to delay the salam accordingly. The text also touches on a dispute: whether exiting the prayer by action is obligatory (which would render the imam's prayer invalid) or not (making it valid); the correct view is that it is not obligatory.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Prohibitively disliked; a ruling that is closer to haram, requiring avoidance and incurring sin if done.
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): Following the imam in all actions of the prayer without preceding or delaying.
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The final sitting in prayer after the last sujud, wherein tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The follower's prayer is invalid.
B) The follower's prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi.
C) The follower's prayer is valid and not disliked.
D) The imam's prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The follower's early salam is prohibitively disliked but valid; exceptions for necessity remove the dislike.

Adhkar After Fard Prayer and the Dispute on Reciting Awrad Between Fard and Sunnah
Explains sunnah of pause after fard and intra-madhhab dispute on awrad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on the recommended pause after fard prayer and identify the positions in the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding reciting awrad between the fard and sunnah prayers.

Core Idea
The recommended pause after fard is sunnah; reciting awrad between fard and sunnah is permissible but better delayed.

This lesson explores the sunnah of pausing briefly after the obligatory prayer with the specific dua before standing for the sunnah, and the intra-madhhab disagreement on whether it is disliked to recite longer litanies (awrad) in between. We will examine the proofs, the differing opinions of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and the author of al-Ikhtiyar, and how later scholars like al-Tahtawi reconcile them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The main act is standing for the sunnah prayer immediately after the fard. The text states this is sunnah. A secondary act is pausing with the dua 'Allahumma anta al-salam...' which is mustahabb (recommended).
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah for immediate connection; mustahabb for the pause.
2
Locate the dalil for the pause
The proof is the Prophet's practice: after salam, he would pause for the duration of that dua. This is narrated in hadith from 'Aishah and others. The text cites this as the basis for the recommended separation.
The pause is not obligatory; it is a recommended action.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on awrad
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said 'la ba's' (no harm) in reciting awrad between fard and sunnah. The author of al-Ikhtiyar said it is disliked (yukrah) to sit and supplicate after a fard that has a sunnah following it.
One opinion denies dislike; the other affirms it.
4
Analyze the tarjih and reconciliation
Al-Tahtawi reconciles by interpreting the dislike in al-Ikhtiyar as tanzihi (lightly disliked), which is essentially the same as 'no harm' (la ba's) meaning permissible but better avoided. The mufta bihi is that it is permissible though better to delay awrad until after the sunnah.
The dislike is not tahrimi; it is only tanzihi.
5
Apply to practice
In practice, a Hanafi may either stand immediately for the sunnah or pause for a brief dua. Reciting longer awrad is allowed, but the better practice is to recite them after the sunnah.
The specific wording of the dua can vary; many adhkar are reported.

Chapter on the description of the remembrances (adhkar) reported after the obligatory prayer, their virtue, and other matters. (Standing for) performing the sunnah that follows the fard immediately after the fard is sunnah, except that it is recommended to separate between them, just as he, peace be upon him, when he made salam, would pause for the duration of saying: 'O Allah, You are Peace, and from You is peace, and to You returns peace.'... He said: ('and other matters') meaning other than what was mentioned, or other than virtue, such as explaining turning, raising the hands during supplication, and wiping the face with them. He said: ('immediately after the fard') the intended meaning of connection is that nothing else intervenes except what will come; this does not contradict his saying 'except that it is recommended' etc. And he did not speak on the separation between sunnah prayers, such as if one prays the after-noon sunnah four rak'ahs and separates between them with a salam; apparently it is recommended not to separate at all, as transmitted. He said: ('just as he, peace be upon him, would...') the 'kaf' is for explanation, i.e., because he would pause, etc. He said: ('O Allah, You are Peace') i.e., possessor of safety from every deficiency; it is a verbal noun used as a predicate for emphasis. He said: ('and from You is peace') i.e., safety from every evil is obtained from You, not from other than You. He said: ('and to You returns peace'). He said in Sharh al-Mishkat from al-Jazari: 'As for what is added after his saying 'and from You is peace', such as 'and to You returns peace... Blessed are You, O Possessor of Majesty and Honor, then he would stand for the sunnah.' Al-Kamal said: 'This is what is established from him of the remembrances that delay the sunnah and separate between it and the fard.' I said: 'Perhaps the intended meaning is other than what is also reported after Maghrib, which is that he would fold his leg and say 'La ilaha illa Allah' ten times, and after Jumu'ah, reciting al-Fatiha and al-Mu'awwidhat seven times each.' And al-Kamal said about Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani that he said: 'There is no harm in reciting awrad (liturgical litanies) between the fard and the sunnah.' So the better approach is to delay the awrad until after the sunnah. This negates dislike, and it is contradicted by what was said in al-Ikhtiyar: 'Every prayer after which there is a sunnah, it is disliked to sit after it and to supplicate.' Rather... (text continues) ... 'Peace, so our Lord with peace, and admit us to the abode of peace' – this has no basis but is fabricated by some storytellers. End. And this is supported by what the author mentioned later from the narration of Muslim. He said: ('Blessed are You') i.e., abundant is Your goodness. He said: ('O Possessor of Majesty') i.e., greatness, which encompasses all virtues. He said: ('and Honor') i.e., bestowal of favors, which is the granting of blessings, and it encompasses all excellences. In the narration of 'A'ishah, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, would not sit except for the duration of saying: 'O Allah, You are Peace...' etc.' This indicates, as the author mentioned, that it is not meant that he would say exactly those words, but rather he would sit for a time that accommodates that amount and similar speech approximately. So it does not contradict what is in the two Sahihs from al-Mughira: 'He would say after every obligatory prayer: 'There is no god but Allah, alone, without partner...' etc.' And this does not contradict what is in Muslim from 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr: 'When the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, finished his prayer, he would say in a loud voice: 'There is no god but Allah...' etc.' because the mentioned duration, in terms of approximation without strict limitation, can accommodate each of these remembrances due to the lack of significant difference between them. It is also derived from the last hadith the permissibility of raising the voice in dhikr and takbir after the obligatory prayers; indeed, some of the Salaf said it is recommended, and Ibn Hazm among the later scholars affirmed it. He said: ('that delay the sunnah') – it is better to restrict to the second sentence. He said: ('I said, perhaps the intended meaning...') I say: Perhaps that (the other narrations) did not reach the strength of the previous hadith, so the people of the madhhab did not explicitly mention it, and goodness lies in following. He said: ('after Maghrib') – it is specified because the sunnah follows it, otherwise similar has been reported for Fajr. He said: ('and al-Mu'awwidhat') – it includes the two mu'awwidhat and al-Samadiyyah (al-Ikhlas). Among its benefits are protection from trials and affliction until the next Friday, an increase of three days, and expiation of all sins, as al-Ajhuri mentioned in Fada'il Ramadan. Know that the previous discussion is when one prays the sunnah in the mosque, for example; but if he intends to go home to perform it, then separation is not disliked even if it exceeds the prescribed amount. He said: ('and it contradicts...') The contradiction is removed by interpreting the dislike mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar as tanzihi (lightly disliked), which is the meaning of al-Halwani's saying 'no harm' because it is used for what is better to avoid, or the dislike in al-Ikhtiyar is interpreted as... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This lesson begins the chapter on the adhkar (remembrances) that are prescribed after the obligatory prayer. The author states that it is sunnah to stand immediately to perform the sunnah prayer that follows the fard (e.g., two rak'ahs after Dhuhr). However, it is mustahabb (recommended) to separate between the fard and sunnah by pausing for a short time, just as the Prophet (peace be upon him) would pause after salam for the duration of saying: 'Allahumma anta al-salam wa minka al-salam wa ilayka ya'ud al-salam' (O Allah, You are Peace, from You is peace, and to You returns peace). The commentary explains the meaning of this dua and notes that other wordings are also reported, such as adding 'Tabarakta ya dha al-jalali wa al-ikram' (Blessed are You, O Possessor of Majesty and Honor). Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam states that this dua is the established one that separates the fard and sunnah. The author then mentions a narration after Maghrib about saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' ten times and after Jumu'ah reciting al-Fatiha and al-Mu'awwidhat seven times each. A key intra-madhhab dispute arises: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said there is no harm (la ba's) in reciting awrad (litanies) between the fard and sunnah prayers, implying it is not makruh. In contrast, the author of al-Ikhtiyar (a Hanafi text) stated that for every prayer that has a sunnah after it, it is disliked (yukrah) to sit and supplicate after the fard (implying one should stand immediately for the sunnah). The commentator (al-Tahtawi) reconciles these views by suggesting that the dislike in al-Ikhtiyar is tanzihi (lightly disliked), which is essentially the same as 'no harm' (la ba's). Alternatively, the statement in al-Ikhtiyar might be about a specific case. The passage also discusses the permissibility of raising the voice in dhikr and takbir after fard prayers, citing a hadith from Ibn al-Zubayr. The overall lesson emphasizes the recommended pause between fard and sunnah but also accommodates various practices, provided one does not innovate.

Key Terms
الأذكار الواردة (al-adhkar al-waridah): The specific remembrances and supplications reported from the Prophet to be recited after the obligatory prayer.
الأوراد (al-awrad): Liturgical litanies or collections of dhikr, often including Quranic verses and supplications, recited at specific times.
الوصل والفصل (al-wasl wa al-fasl): ‘Wasi’ means connecting the sunnah to the fard without delay; ‘fasl’ means separating them with a pause or other actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Tahtawi's commentary, what is the status of reciting awrad between the fard and sunnah prayer?
A) It is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
B) It is permissible (ja'iz) but better to delay until after sunnah.
C) It is obligatory to do so.
D) It invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends a brief pause after fard with the dua 'Allahumma anta al-salam...' but allows reciting awrad between fard and sunnah, though delaying them to after the sunnah is better.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Optimal Sequence After Obligatory Prayer
Ruling on post-fard sequence and hadith analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi regarding the sequence between fard and sunnah and apply the hadith of Aisha to justify it.

Core Idea
Sit briefly for supplication, then stand immediately for sunnah — this is the established Prophetic practice.

After completing the obligatory prayer, the worshipper faces a choice: supplicate, recite litanies, or proceed directly to the sunnah prayer. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the recommended sequence, clarifying that the Prophet ﷺ would sit only briefly for a concise dhikr such as 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam' before standing for the sunnah. We will explore the primary evidence and reconcile apparent contradictions in the hadith literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage focuses on the interval between fard and sunnah. Identify the recommended act (mustahabb) and the disliked act (makruh tanzihi).
The ruling is mustahabb for brief supplication, makruh tanzihi for lengthy interruption.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Aisha (RA) cited in the text: 'The Prophet ﷺ would not sit except for the duration of saying: Allahumma Anta as-Salam…'
This hadith is from Muslim and is ahad, but its meaning is clear.
3
Establish the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the phrase 'لا يقعد إلا مقدار' proves a brief pause — the Prophet sat only as long as it takes to say those words, then stood.
The imperative implied by action (fi'l) is considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
4
Reconcile conflicting narrations
The passage lists other authentic narrations with longer supplications (e.g., from al-Mughirah, Ibn al-Zubayr). Explain that the 'duration' is approximate and can accommodate various phrasings.
Al-Tahtawi argues no real contradiction because the Prophet sat for an approximate time, not an exact fixed supplication.
5
Extract the mufta bihi
State the operative ruling: sit briefly for 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam' (or equivalent), then stand for sunnah. Lengthy awrad should be delayed until after sunnah.
This is the relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school.

سواء البيت، أو غيره (ويستحب للإمام بعد سلامه أن يتحول إلى يمين القبلة وهو الجانب المقابل (إلى جهة يساره) أي يسار المستقبل لأن يمين المقابل جهة يسار المستقبل فيتحول إليه (التطوع بعد الفرض) لأن لليمين فضلاً ولدفع الاشتباه نظنه في الفرض فيقتدي به وكذلك للقوم، ذلك التحريم، ويحمل على الأدعية الطويلة، وحينئذ يكون ما قاله الحلواني : محمولاً على الفصل بنحو : اللهم أنت السلام ولا بأس مستعملة في مطلق الجواز. قوله: (والدعاء) هذا لا ينافي الإتيان باللهم أنت السلام الخ لأنه ليس دعاء بل ثناء إلا أن يراد بالدعاء ما . الذكر أو هو يعم بالنظر إلى قوله فحيناً الخ دعاء على ما فيه قوله : (وعن عائشة الخ ) . ا هو من جملة ما في الاختيار كما يفيده كلامه في كبيره وحينئذ فتحمل الكراهة على الإتيان بما هو أزيد من أو المراد بالدعاء حقيقته وهو أحد الاحتمالين السابقين. قوله : (بما ليس من توابع الصلاة) كأكل وشرب. قوله : (وقد أشرنا الخ) لا تفهم تلك الإشارة مما سبق لأن ما سبق في الفصل بالأوراد، وهذا في الفصل بالكلام الكثير ولا يفهم حكم أحدهما من الآخر . قوله : (إلى أنه إذا تكلم الخ) مثل ذلك ما إذا أخر السنة إلى آخر الوقت على الأصح وقيل لا تكون سنة وظاهر القبلية والبعدية، والأفضل الوصل فيهما قوله : (أداؤها فيما هو أبعد . الرياء) أي ما عدا التراويح فإن الأفضل فيها المسجد أفاده الشرح وما عدا تحية المسجد. قوله: (وأجمع للخلوص) أي أكثر إخلاصاً وهو أعم مما قبله قوله : (أو غيره أو بمعنى الواو لأن التسوية لا تقع إلا بين متعدد وأو لأحد الشيئين أو الأشياء وفي نسخ بالواو قوله: (لأن لليمين فضلاً) هذا علة لمحذوف أي وإنما اختير يمين القبلة عن يسارها وإن كان جائزاً الآن الخ. قوله : (ولدفع الاشتباء الخ) هذه العلة لأصل التحول لا لكونه لجهة اليمين فالأولى ذكرها عند قوله أن يتحول قوله: (وكذلك للقوم) أي وكذلك يستحب للقوم وهو عطف على قوله، ويستحب للإمام ودليله ما روى أبو هريرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : أيعجز أحدكم أن يتقدم أو يتأخر أو عن يمينه أو من شماله في الصلاة ا يعني في السبحة رواه أبو داود وابن ماجه
Blessed are You, O Possessor of Majesty and Honor, then he stands for the sunnah. Al-Kamal said: This is what is established from him of the remembrances that delay the sunnah, and by which he separates between it and the obligatory prayer. I said: Perhaps what is meant is other than what is also established after Maghrib, which is (while shifting his foot) 'La ilaha illa Allah' ten times, and after Jumu'ah, reciting al-Fatihah and al-Mu'awwidhat seven times each. (And) al-Kamal said (from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani) that he said: 'There is no harm in reciting litanies between the obligatory prayer and the sunnah.' So the better is to delay the litanies until after the sunnah. This negates the dislike (karahah), and it contradicts what was said in al-Ikhtiyar: 'Every prayer after which there is a sunnah, it is disliked to sit after it and make supplication.' Rather, 'as-Salamu hayyana rabbana...' has no basis, but is fabricated by some storytellers. This is supported by what the author mentioned later from the narration of Muslim. His saying: 'Tabarakta' meaning abundant is Your goodness. His saying: 'Ya dha al-Jalali' meaning majesty, which encompasses all virtues. His saying: 'wa al-Ikram' meaning bestowal of favors, which is granting blessings, encompassing all excellences. In a narration from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not sit except for the duration of saying: Allahumma Anta as-Salam...' This indicates, as the author mentioned, that it is not that he said those exact words, but he would sit for a time that would accommodate that amount or similar words approximately. So it does not contradict what is in the two Sahihs from al-Mughirah that he used to say after every prescribed prayer: 'La ilaha illa Allah wahdahu...' nor what is in Muslim from Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr that the Prophet (peace be upon him) after finishing his prayer would say in a loud voice: 'La ilaha illa Allah...' because the mentioned approximate amount can accommodate each of these remembrances due to lack of great difference between them. From the last hadith, one can derive the permissibility of raising the voice in dhikr and takbir after obligatory prayers; indeed, some predecessors said it is recommended, and Ibn Hazm among the later scholars asserted it. His saying: 'which delay the sunnah' – the better is to restrict to the second phrase. His saying: 'I said: perhaps what is meant' I say: perhaps that is not as strong as the previous hadith, hence the people of the madhhab did not specify it, and goodness lies in following. His saying: 'after Maghrib' – it is specifically mentioned because the sunnah follows it, otherwise a similar report has come for Fajr. His saying: 'and al-Mu'awwidhat' – it includes the two Mu'awwidhat by predominance over al-Samadiyyah. Among its fruits is protection from trials and afflictions until the next Friday, plus an increase of three days, and expiation of all sins as mentioned by al-Ujhuri in Fada'il Ramadan. Know that the previous discussion applies when one prays the sunnah in the mosque, for example. But if he intends to go home to perform it, then separating is not disliked even if it exceeds the prescribed amount. His saying: 'and it contradicts it' – the contradiction is removed by interpreting the dislike (karahah) mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar as tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited), which is the meaning of al-Halwani's saying 'la ba's' (no harm), because 'la ba's' is used for things whose opposite is better. Or by interpreting what is in al-Ikhtiyar as referring to dislike of engaging in the sunnah so as not to separate between the sunnah and the obligatory prayer. From Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to sit for the duration of saying 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam...' as previously mentioned, so he would not exceed that or its equivalent. Then al-Kamal said: It is not established from her the separation with the remembrances that are regularly practiced in mosques in our time, such as reciting Ayat al-Kursi, the tasbihat and their likes thirty-three times and others. And the Prophet's saying: 'The poor emigrants, glorify Allah, say Allahu Akbar, and praise Him after every prayer...' necessitates connecting them to the obligatory prayer. Rather, their being after the sunnah without engaging in what is not from the appendages of prayer makes them correctly considered 'after it' (dubur). And we have indicated that if one speaks a lot, or eats or drinks between the obligatory prayer and the sunnah, it does not invalidate (the sunnah) – this is the most correct view – rather, its reward is diminished. And the best for performing the sunan is to do them in a place farthest from ostentation and most conducive to sincerity, whether at home or elsewhere. (It is recommended for the imam after his salam to turn to the right side of the qibla, which is the opposite side (to the direction of his left) i.e. the left of the person facing the qibla, because the right of the opposite side is the left of the one facing, so he turns to it (for voluntary prayer after the obligatory prayer) because the right has virtue and to avoid confusion, we think he is in the obligatory prayer and they follow him. Similarly for the congregation. That is the ruling for prohibition, and it applies to lengthy supplications. Then what al-Halwani said is interpreted as separation with something like 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam' and 'la ba's' is used for absolute permissibility. His saying: '(and supplication) – this does not contradict coming with 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam' because it is not supplication but praise, unless by supplication is meant dhikr, or it is general considering his saying 'hayyana' etc. is a supplication as per what is in it. His saying: '(from Aisha) – it is part of what is in al-Ikhtiyar as indicated by his words in his larger work. Then the dislike is interpreted as coming with something more than that, or by 'supplication' is meant its literal meaning, which is one of the two previous possibilities. His saying: '(with what is not from the appendices of prayer)' such as eating and drinking. His saying: '(and we have indicated)' – do not understand that indication from what preceded, because what preceded was about separating with litanies, and this is about separating with much speech, and the ruling of one cannot be understood from the other. His saying: '(that if he speaks)' – similar to that is if he delays the sunnah until the end of its time, according to the most correct view; and it was said it is not a sunnah, and the apparent view of precedence and posteriority, and the better is to connect in both. His saying: '(performing them in a place farthest from ostentation)' – this excludes tarawih, for which the mosque is better, as stated in the Sharh, and excludes tahiyyat al-masjid. His saying: '(and most conducive to sincerity)' meaning more sincere, and it is more general than what precedes it. His saying: '(or other than it)' – 'aw' is in the sense of 'waw' because equality can only occur between multiple things, and 'aw' is for one of two things or things; in some copies it is with 'waw'. His saying: '(because the right has virtue)' – this is the cause for an omitted phrase: i.e., the right side of the qibla is chosen over its left, although it is permissible now... etc. His saying: '(and to avoid confusion)' – this cause is for the original turning, not for specifically turning to the right side; so it would have been better to mention it at his saying 'that he turns'. His saying: '(and similarly for the congregation)' meaning similarly it is recommended for the congregation, and it is a conjunction to his saying 'it is recommended for the imam', and its proof is what Abu Hurairah narrated: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Is one of you unable to step forward or backward or to his right or left in prayer?' meaning in the supererogatory prayer. Narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of Maraqi al-Falah regarding the rulings after the obligatory prayer. The author discusses the proper sequence of post-prayer acts: the optimal practice is to briefly sit for a concise supplication (such as 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam') and then immediately stand for the sunnah prayer. He cites Kamal ibn al-Humam and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, who state that reciting litanies (awrad) between fard and sunnah is permissible (la ba's), but delaying them until after the sunnah is preferable. This negates any strict dislike. However, a contradictory view in al-Ikhtiyar says it is disliked to sit and supplicate after prayers that have a sunnah. The commentator resolves this by interpreting the dislike as tanzihi (light dislike) and clarifying that the prohibition applies only to lengthy supplications, not to brief ones like 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam'. The passage then examines various hadith reports about the Prophet's post-prayer supplications, showing they are all compatible because the Prophet would sit for a short time approximate to these phrases. It also derives the permissibility of raising the voice in dhikr and takbir after prayers. The commentator then addresses the practice of reciting specific surahs and tasbihat after prayers, noting that while common in mosques, they are not directly established from the Prophet's practice; rather, the established practice is to connect the sunnah closely to the fard. Speaking, eating, or drinking between fard and sunnah does not invalidate the sunnah but reduces its reward. Finally, the text discusses the recommendation for the imam to turn to his right (the side opposite the qibla's left) after salam for voluntary prayer, to avoid confusion and because the right side has virtue, citing a hadith from Abu Hurairah.

Key Terms
التطوع بعد الفرض (al-tatawwu' ba'd al-fard): Voluntary (sunnah or nafl) prayer performed after the obligatory prayer.
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): A light dislike (makruh tanzihi), meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Aisha (RA), how long did the Prophet ﷺ sit after the fard prayer before standing for sunnah?
A) He did not sit at all.
B) He sat for the duration of saying 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam'.
C) He sat for a long time reciting tasbihat.
D) He sat until the congregation left.

Key Takeaway
The optimal Sunnah after fard is a brief pause for a concise supplication, then immediate standing for the sunnah prayer.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Resolving the Dispute on Litanies (Awrad) Between Fard and Sunnah
Resolution of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on awrad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi resolution of the ikhtilaf between al-Halwani and al-Ikhtiyar regarding litanies after fard, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Litanies between fard and sunnah are permissible but delaying them is better — the 'dislike' is tanzihi, not tahrimi.

A common practice in many mosques is to recite communal litanies (awrad) such as Ayat al-Kursi and tasbihat immediately after the fard prayer, before the sunnah. This practice has been the subject of debate within the Hanafi school. In this passage, al-Tahtawi records the positions of al-Halwani (no harm) and al-Ikhtiyar (disliked) and resolves the apparent contradiction. He also addresses the ruling on other intervening acts like speaking or eating, and the recommendation for the imam to turn to the right for voluntary prayer. This lesson focuses on the method of resolving the ikhtilaf and the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting positions
Locate the two statements: al-Halwani says 'لا بأس بقراءة الأوراد بين الفريضة والسنة' (no harm in reciting litanies between fard and sunnah) and al-Ikhtiyar says 'يكره القعود بعدها والدعاء' (it is disliked to sit after it and make supplication).
These appear to contradict each other.
2
Analyze the resolution method
Al-Tahtawi offers two ways to remove the contradiction: (1) interpret the karahah in al-Ikhtiyar as tanzihi (light dislike), which aligns with 'la ba's' meaning 'permissible but its opposite is better'; (2) interpret the karahah as referring to lengthy supplications only.
The key is to limit the application of 'disliked' to excessive acts.
3
Apply the resolution to the practice
Understand that the mufta bihi is: brief supplication (like 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam') is recommended; longer awrad are permissible but delaying them until after sunnah is better. The dislike is only tanzihi and does not invalidate the sunnah.
This reconciles the two views.
4
Examine the evidence for the resolution
The hadith of Aisha and the Prophet's practice of sitting only a short time support the mufta bihi. The fact that the Prophet said 'الفقراء المهاجرين تسبحون وتكبرون' after every prayer but the word 'دبر' can mean after the sunnah as well, is also considered.
The passage also notes that speaking/eating/drinking does not invalidate the sunnah but reduces reward.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if someone recites lengthy awrad between fard and sunnah, their sunnah is valid but they have committed a makruh tanzihi act. The better path is to follow the brief model.
This avoids extremism and keeps the practice within the scope of permissibility.

لما منعت، ولا ينفع ذا الجد منك الجد، وهذا لا ينافي ما في مسلم عن عبد الله بن الزبير كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا فرغ من صلاته قال بصوته الأعلى: لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، له الملك وله الحمد وهو على كل شيء قدير ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم، ولا نعبد إلا إياه وله الفضل وله الثناء الحسن لا إله إلا الله مخصلين له الدين، ولو كره الكافرون، لأن المقدار المذكور من حيث التقريب دون عائشة أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقعد مقدار ما يقول اللهم أنت السلام الخ كما تقدم فلا يزيد عليه أو على قدره، ثم قال الكمال، ولم يثبت عنها الفصل بالأذكار التي يواظب عليها في المساجد في عصرنا من ليس من توابع الصلاة فصح كونها ،دبرها، وقد أشرنا إلى أنه إذا تكلم بكلام كثير ، أو أكل أو شرب بين الفرض والسنة لا تبطل وهو الأصح، بل نقص ثوابها والأفضل بالسنن أداؤها فيما هو أبعد من الرياء، وأجمع للخلوص الجواز. قوله: (والدعاء) هذا لا ينافي الإتيان باللهم أنت السلام الخ لأنه ليس دعاء بل ثناء إلا أن يراد بالدعاء ما . الذكر أو هو يعم بالنظر إلى قوله فحيناً الخ دعاء على ما فيه قوله : (وعن عائشة الخ ) . ا هو من جملة ما في الاختيار كما يفيده كلامه في كبيره وحينئذ فتحمل الكراهة على الإتيان بما هو أزيد من أو المراد بالدعاء حقيقته وهو أحد الاحتمالين السابقين. قوله : (بما ليس من توابع الصلاة) كأكل وشرب. قوله : (وقد أشرنا الخ) لا تفهم تلك الإشارة مما سبق لأن ما سبق في الفصل بالأوراد، وهذا في الفصل بالكلام الكثير ولا يفهم حكم أحدهما من الآخر . قوله : (إلى أنه إذا تكلم الخ) مثل ذلك ما إذا أخر السنة إلى آخر الوقت على الأصح وقيل لا تكون سنة وظاهر القبلية والبعدية، والأفضل الوصل فيهما قوله : (أداؤها فيما هو أبعد . الرياء) أي ما عدا التراويح فإن الأفضل فيها المسجد أفاده الشرح وما عدا تحية المسجد. قوله: (وأجمع للخلوص) أي أكثر إخلاصاً وهو أعم مما قبله قوله : (أو غيره أو بمعنى الواو لأن التسوية لا تقع إلا بين متعدد وأو لأحد الشيئين أو الأشياء وفي نسخ بالواو قوله: (لأن لليمين فضلاً) هذا علة لمحذوف أي وإنما اختير يمين القبلة عن يسارها وإن كان جائزاً الآن الخ. قوله : (ولدفع الاشتباء الخ) هذه العلة لأصل التحول لا لكونه لجهة اليمين فالأولى ذكرها عند قوله أن يتحول قوله: (وكذلك للقوم) أي وكذلك يستحب للقوم وهو عطف على قوله، ويستحب للإمام ودليله ما روى أبو هريرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : أيعجز أحدكم أن يتقدم أو يتأخر أو عن يمينه أو من شماله في الصلاة ا يعني في السبحة رواه أبو داود وابن ماجه
Blessed are You, O Possessor of Majesty and Honor, then he stands for the sunnah. Al-Kamal said: This is what is established from him of the remembrances that delay the sunnah, and by which he separates between it and the obligatory prayer. I said: Perhaps what is meant is other than what is also established after Maghrib, which is (while shifting his foot) 'La ilaha illa Allah' ten times, and after Jumu'ah, reciting al-Fatihah and al-Mu'awwidhat seven times each. (And) al-Kamal said (from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani) that he said: 'There is no harm in reciting litanies between the obligatory prayer and the sunnah.' So the better is to delay the litanies until after the sunnah. This negates the dislike (karahah), and it contradicts what was said in al-Ikhtiyar: 'Every prayer after which there is a sunnah, it is disliked to sit after it and make supplication.' Rather, 'as-Salamu hayyana rabbana...' has no basis, but is fabricated by some storytellers. This is supported by what the author mentioned later from the narration of Muslim. His saying: 'Tabarakta' meaning abundant is Your goodness. His saying: 'Ya dha al-Jalali' meaning majesty, which encompasses all virtues. His saying: 'wa al-Ikram' meaning bestowal of favors, which is granting blessings, encompassing all excellences. In a narration from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not sit except for the duration of saying: Allahumma Anta as-Salam...' This indicates, as the author mentioned, that it is not that he said those exact words, but he would sit for a time that would accommodate that amount or similar words approximately. So it does not contradict what is in the two Sahihs from al-Mughirah that he used to say after every prescribed prayer: 'La ilaha illa Allah wahdahu...' nor what is in Muslim from Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr that the Prophet (peace be upon him) after finishing his prayer would say in a loud voice: 'La ilaha illa Allah...' because the mentioned approximate amount can accommodate each of these remembrances due to lack of great difference between them. From the last hadith, one can derive the permissibility of raising the voice in dhikr and takbir after obligatory prayers; indeed, some predecessors said it is recommended, and Ibn Hazm among the later scholars asserted it. His saying: 'which delay the sunnah' – the better is to restrict to the second phrase. His saying: 'I said: perhaps what is meant' I say: perhaps that is not as strong as the previous hadith, hence the people of the madhhab did not specify it, and goodness lies in following. His saying: 'after Maghrib' – it is specifically mentioned because the sunnah follows it, otherwise a similar report has come for Fajr. His saying: 'and al-Mu'awwidhat' – it includes the two Mu'awwidhat by predominance over al-Samadiyyah. Among its fruits is protection from trials and afflictions until the next Friday, plus an increase of three days, and expiation of all sins as mentioned by al-Ujhuri in Fada'il Ramadan. Know that the previous discussion applies when one prays the sunnah in the mosque, for example. But if he intends to go home to perform it, then separating is not disliked even if it exceeds the prescribed amount. His saying: 'and it contradicts it' – the contradiction is removed by interpreting the dislike (karahah) mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar as tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited), which is the meaning of al-Halwani's saying 'la ba's' (no harm), because 'la ba's' is used for things whose opposite is better. Or by interpreting what is in al-Ikhtiyar as referring to dislike of engaging in the sunnah so as not to separate between the sunnah and the obligatory prayer. From Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to sit for the duration of saying 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam...' as previously mentioned, so he would not exceed that or its equivalent. Then al-Kamal said: It is not established from her the separation with the remembrances that are regularly practiced in mosques in our time, such as reciting Ayat al-Kursi, the tasbihat and their likes thirty-three times and others. And the Prophet's saying: 'The poor emigrants, glorify Allah, say Allahu Akbar, and praise Him after every prayer...' necessitates connecting them to the obligatory prayer. Rather, their being after the sunnah without engaging in what is not from the appendages of prayer makes them correctly considered 'after it' (dubur). And we have indicated that if one speaks a lot, or eats or drinks between the obligatory prayer and the sunnah, it does not invalidate (the sunnah) – this is the most correct view – rather, its reward is diminished. And the best for performing the sunan is to do them in a place farthest from ostentation and most conducive to sincerity, whether at home or elsewhere. (It is recommended for the imam after his salam to turn to the right side of the qibla, which is the opposite side (to the direction of his left) i.e. the left of the person facing the qibla, because the right of the opposite side is the left of the one facing, so he turns to it (for voluntary prayer after the obligatory prayer) because the right has virtue and to avoid confusion, we think he is in the obligatory prayer and they follow him. Similarly for the congregation. That is the ruling for prohibition, and it applies to lengthy supplications. Then what al-Halwani said is interpreted as separation with something like 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam' and 'la ba's' is used for absolute permissibility. His saying: '(and supplication) – this does not contradict coming with 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam' because it is not supplication but praise, unless by supplication is meant dhikr, or it is general considering his saying 'hayyana' etc. is a supplication as per what is in it. His saying: '(from Aisha) – it is part of what is in al-Ikhtiyar as indicated by his words in his larger work. Then the dislike is interpreted as coming with something more than that, or by 'supplication' is meant its literal meaning, which is one of the two previous possibilities. His saying: '(with what is not from the appendices of prayer)' such as eating and drinking. His saying: '(and we have indicated)' – do not understand that indication from what preceded, because what preceded was about separating with litanies, and this is about separating with much speech, and the ruling of one cannot be understood from the other. His saying: '(that if he speaks)' – similar to that is if he delays the sunnah until the end of its time, according to the most correct view; and it was said it is not a sunnah, and the apparent view of precedence and posteriority, and the better is to connect in both. His saying: '(performing them in a place farthest from ostentation)' – this excludes tarawih, for which the mosque is better, as stated in the Sharh, and excludes tahiyyat al-masjid. His saying: '(and most conducive to sincerity)' meaning more sincere, and it is more general than what precedes it. His saying: '(or other than it)' – 'aw' is in the sense of 'waw' because equality can only occur between multiple things, and 'aw' is for one of two things or things; in some copies it is with 'waw'. His saying: '(because the right has virtue)' – this is the cause for an omitted phrase: i.e., the right side of the qibla is chosen over its left, although it is permissible now... etc. His saying: '(and to avoid confusion)' – this cause is for the original turning, not for specifically turning to the right side; so it would have been better to mention it at his saying 'that he turns'. His saying: '(and similarly for the congregation)' meaning similarly it is recommended for the congregation, and it is a conjunction to his saying 'it is recommended for the imam', and its proof is what Abu Hurairah narrated: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Is one of you unable to step forward or backward or to his right or left in prayer?' meaning in the supererogatory prayer. Narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of Maraqi al-Falah regarding the rulings after the obligatory prayer. The author discusses the proper sequence of post-prayer acts: the optimal practice is to briefly sit for a concise supplication (such as 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam') and then immediately stand for the sunnah prayer. He cites Kamal ibn al-Humam and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, who state that reciting litanies (awrad) between fard and sunnah is permissible (la ba's), but delaying them until after the sunnah is preferable. This negates any strict dislike. However, a contradictory view in al-Ikhtiyar says it is disliked to sit and supplicate after prayers that have a sunnah. The commentator resolves this by interpreting the dislike as tanzihi (light dislike) and clarifying that the prohibition applies only to lengthy supplications, not to brief ones like 'Allahumma Anta as-Salam'. The passage then examines various hadith reports about the Prophet's post-prayer supplications, showing they are all compatible because the Prophet would sit for a short time approximate to these phrases. It also derives the permissibility of raising the voice in dhikr and takbir after prayers. The commentator then addresses the practice of reciting specific surahs and tasbihat after prayers, noting that while common in mosques, they are not directly established from the Prophet's practice; rather, the established practice is to connect the sunnah closely to the fard. Speaking, eating, or drinking between fard and sunnah does not invalidate the sunnah but reduces its reward. Finally, the text discusses the recommendation for the imam to turn to his right (the side opposite the qibla's left) after salam for voluntary prayer, to avoid confusion and because the right side has virtue, citing a hadith from Abu Hurairah.

Key Terms
الأوراد (al-awrad): Litanies or regular recitations, including specific surahs and tasbihat, recited after prayers.
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): A light dislike (makruh tanzihi), meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does al-Tahtawi resolve the conflict between al-Halwani and al-Ikhtiyar?
A) He rejects al-Ikhtiyar as a weak opinion.
B) He interprets the karahah in al-Ikhtiyar as tanzihi and limits it to lengthy supplications.
C) He says both opinions are correct and leaves the choice to the individual.
D) He argues that the hadith evidence overrides both opinions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the apparent conflict by categorizing lengthy litanies between fard and sunnah as makruh tanzihi, while a brief supplication remains mustahabb.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Performing the Sunnah Immediately After Fard
Ruling on connecting sunnah to fard and effect of intervening actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the sunnah should be performed right after the fard without intervening dhikr, and explain that speaking or eating between reduces reward but does not invalidate.

Core Idea
Connect the sunnah to the fard without delay; separate dhikr after sunnah is sunnah, not between.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah explains the proper sequence after the obligatory prayer. The Prophet's practice was to sit only long enough to say 'Allahumma anta al-salam' and then immediately pray the sunnah. Many Muslims today recite long litanies between the fard and sunnah, but this is not from the established sunnah. The passage also clarifies that if one speaks, eats, or drinks between the two, the prayer remains valid, though the reward is diminished.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the sunnah prayer after the fard. Its ruling is sunnah muakkadah (highly recommended).
2
Locate the dalil from Aisha
Aisha reported that the Prophet would sit only for the duration of 'Allahumma anta al-salam.' This indicates that the sunnah should be performed immediately after the fard.
The hadith shows brevity.
3
Understand the meaning of 'dubur al-salah'
The hadith 'you glorify, magnify, and praise after every prayer' (dubur kulli salatin) refers to after the sunnah if performed, or after the fard if no sunnah. So the dhikr is after the sunnah, not between.
4
Apply the ruling on speaking/eating between
If one speaks a lot, eats, or drinks between the fard and sunnah, the prayer (sunnah) is still valid but the reward is less. This is the most correct opinion.
It does not invalidate.
5
Determine the preferred place
The best is to perform the sunnah where it is further from ostentation and more conducive to sincerity, whether at home or elsewhere.
For tarawih and tahiyyat al-masjid, the mosque is best.

His saying: (and likewise for the congregation) i.e., it is recommended for the congregation, and it is a conjunction on his saying 'and it is recommended for the imam', and its proof is what Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Is any of you unable to step forward, step back, or to his right or left in prayer?' meaning in the supererogatory prayer. Reported by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah. And some of our shaykhs said: There is no sin on them in omitting the turning because there is no confusion for the one entering upon seeing the imam's place empty. His saying: (based on the narration that the place of the one praying etc.) Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) recited that day: 'It will relate its news' (99:4). He said: 'Do you know what its news are?' They said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: 'Its news are that it will testify for every male and female servant regarding what they did on its surface. It will say: he did such and such on such day.' Reported by al-Tirmidhi and he said: hasan sahih. And al-Qurtubi narrated in the interpretation of His statement: 'And the heaven and the earth did not weep for them' (44:29) from Ali and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that the earth weeps for the believer for his place of prayer and his place of ascension of his deeds. And the interpretation of the verse on this is: 'So the places of ascension of their deeds from the heaven and the places of their worship from the earth did not weep for them.' Hence, Ata al-Khurasani said: No servant prostrates to Allah Almighty in any spot of the earth except that it will testify for him on the Day of Resurrection and weep for him on the day he dies. Quoted from Ibn Amir Hajj summarized. His saying: (and it is recommended to face after it etc.) whether the congregation is ten or less, contrary to those who differentiate, and a fabricated hadith is reported about that. And his action, like others, indicates that the imam is allowed after finishing the voluntary or the obligatory if there is no voluntary after it: if he wishes he turns to his right, if he wishes to his left, if he wishes he goes to his needs, and if he wishes he faces the people with his face. Know that these four are different from the turning for the voluntary because he does it after it, so ponder. His saying: (if there is not someone praying in front of him) for if there is, it is disliked due to what is in the two Sahihs: Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) disliked that a man face another while he is praying. And Iyad narrated it from the generality of scholars, and they did not differentiate between whether the praying person is in the first row or the last, and that is the apparent position of the madhhab, even if there are rows between them, because the imam's sitting facing him, even if far, is like sitting before him. Ibn Amir Hajj said: What appears is that if between the imam and the one praying facing him there is a man sitting with his back to the face of the praying person, it is not disliked for the imam to face the people because in this state, it is not disliked to pass in front of the praying person due to that man interposing between him and the praying person. So similarly, here he becomes an interceptor for facing those behind him. He said: Perhaps Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) only did not mention this condition due to its being known. His saying: (And the command is for permission (ibaha)) the origin of this statement is from al-Halabi, and its completion is in it. And they seek forgiveness from Allah the Almighty three times (three times) due to the saying of Thawban: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), when he finished his prayer, would seek forgiveness from Allah the Almighty three times and say: 'O Allah, You are Peace...'
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses several post-fard prayer rulings. It begins with the recommendation to engage in the sunnah immediately after the fard to avoid separation. The author cites Aisha's hadith that the Prophet would sit only for the duration of saying 'Allahumma anta al-salam' (O Allah, You are Peace), and he did not add the regular dhikr now common in mosques like Ayat al-Kursi and tasbihat. The hadith 'the poor emigrants will glorify Allah after every prayer' indicates that these glorifications are to be connected to the fard, not separated. However, if one speaks, eats, or drinks between the fard and sunnah, the prayer is not invalidated (it remains valid but the reward is less). The preferable way is to perform sunnah in a place more conducive to sincerity. Then the ruling: it is recommended for the imam after salam to move to the right side of the qibla (i.e., towards the left of the person facing qibla) to perform the sunnah, because the right has virtue and to avoid confusion for the congregation. Likewise for the congregation. The passage then clarifies that the dislike (karaha) of long supplications applies only to excessive ones, not to short ones like 'Allahumma anta al-salam.' It explains that 'supplication' here may include praise like 'Allahumma anta al-salam.' The author discusses the meaning of 'what is not from the accompaniments of prayer' such as eating and drinking, and indicates that the earlier reference to separation with litanies is different from talking. Then the recommendation for the imam to turn to face the people after finishing the sunnah (or fard if no sunnah) is mentioned; he may turn right or left, go about his needs, or face the congregation. This is based on hadith and the practice of the Prophet. The imam should not face someone who is praying directly, but if there is a barrier (like a sitting person whose back is to the worshiper), it is not disliked. Finally, the istighfar (seeking forgiveness) three times after prayer is confirmed from Thawban and is a recommended sunnah.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): The voluntary prayers performed after the obligatory five daily prayers.
دبر الصلاة (dubur al-salah): Literally 'the back of the prayer', meaning immediately after the fard, but here specifically after the sunnah if performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person speaks a lot between the fard and sunnah prayer?
A) The fard prayer becomes invalid.
B) The sunnah prayer is invalid.
C) The sunnah prayer remains valid but reward is diminished.
D) Both prayers become invalid.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah prayer should be performed immediately after the fard without intervening dhikr; eating or drinking between reduces reward but does not invalidate.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Imam's Turning and Post-Prayer Supplications
Rulings on imam's turning, facing congregation, and post-prayer dhikr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the recommended actions for the imam after the prayer, including turning to the right for sunnah, facing the congregation, and reciting istighfar three times.

Core Idea
The imam should turn to the right to pray sunnah, then may face the congregation; istighfar three times is a confirmed sunnah.

This passage continues with the post-fard sunnah, focusing on the imam's actions after salam. It is recommended for the imam to move to the right of the qibla to perform the voluntary prayer, to avoid confusion for the congregation. After finishing the sunnah (or fard if no sunnah), he may face the people, turn to his right or left, or go about his needs. The passage also discusses the ruling on facing someone who is praying and confirms the sunnah of seeking forgiveness three times and saying 'Allahumma anta al-salam'.

Guided Path
1
State the recommendation for the imam's turning
It is mustahabb for the imam after salam to move to the right of the qibla (which is the left of the person facing qibla) to perform the sunnah.
This is to avoid confusion and because the right side has virtue.
2
Identify the ruling for the congregation
It is also mustahabb for the congregation to turn similarly, based on the hadith of Abu Huraira about moving forward, backward, or to the sides in supererogatory prayer.
3
Understand the conditions for facing the congregation
After completing the prayers, the imam may face the people, turn right or left, or leave. However, he should not face someone who is still praying directly if there is no barrier.
4
Note the istighfar after prayer
It is recommended to seek forgiveness three times after finishing the prayer, based on the hadith of Thawban: the Prophet would say 'Astaghfirullah' three times and then 'Allahumma anta al-salam'.
This is a sunnah regardless of whether one is imam or follower.
5
Recognize the difference between supplication and praise
The phrase 'Allahumma anta al-salam' is praise, not supplication, so it does not contradict the recommendation to make supplication after prayer.

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses several post-fard prayer rulings. It begins with the recommendation to engage in the sunnah immediately after the fard to avoid separation. The author cites Aisha's hadith that the Prophet would sit only for the duration of saying 'Allahumma anta al-salam' (O Allah, You are Peace), and he did not add the regular dhikr now common in mosques like Ayat al-Kursi and tasbihat. The hadith 'the poor emigrants will glorify Allah after every prayer' indicates that these glorifications are to be connected to the fard, not separated. However, if one speaks, eats, or drinks between the fard and sunnah, the prayer is not invalidated (it remains valid but the reward is less). The preferable way is to perform sunnah in a place more conducive to sincerity. Then the ruling: it is recommended for the imam after salam to move to the right side of the qibla (i.e., towards the left of the person facing qibla) to perform the sunnah, because the right has virtue and to avoid confusion for the congregation. Likewise for the congregation. The passage then clarifies that the dislike (karaha) of long supplications applies only to excessive ones, not to short ones like 'Allahumma anta al-salam.' It explains that 'supplication' here may include praise like 'Allahumma anta al-salam.' The author discusses the meaning of 'what is not from the accompaniments of prayer' such as eating and drinking, and indicates that the earlier reference to separation with litanies is different from talking. Then the recommendation for the imam to turn to face the people after finishing the sunnah (or fard if no sunnah) is mentioned; he may turn right or left, go about his needs, or face the congregation. This is based on hadith and the practice of the Prophet. The imam should not face someone who is praying directly, but if there is a barrier (like a sitting person whose back is to the worshiper), it is not disliked. Finally, the istighfar (seeking forgiveness) three times after prayer is confirmed from Thawban and is a recommended sunnah.

Key Terms
التحول (al-tahawwul): The imam moving from his place after the fard prayer to sit and pray the sunnah elsewhere, typically to the right side.
استقبال الناس (istiqbal al-nas): The imam turning to face the congregation after completing all prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Sunnah regarding istighfar after the prayer?

Key Takeaway
The imam should turn to the right for sunnah, may face the congregation afterwards, and it is sunnah to seek forgiveness three times after prayer.

Post-Prayer Sunan: Facing Congregation, Istighfar, Ayat al-Kursi, Mu'awwidhat, and Tasbihat
Lists recommended post-prayer sunan with proofs and scholarly refinements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify all recommended actions after obligatory prayers according to the Hanafi school, cite the prophetic proofs for each, and explain the flexibility in order and numbers of tasbihat.

Core Idea
Post-prayer dhikr is strongly recommended; its multiple forms and numbers are all valid and reflect prophetic practice.

After completing the obligatory prayer, a series of sunan acts are recommended based on the Prophet's consistent practice. This lesson walks through each action—the imam's turning, istighfar, reciting Ayat al-Kursi and al-Mu'awwidhat, and the tasbihat—with their specific proofs and the Hanafi position on their flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify each recommended act
Read the passage and list the five main categories: imam facing congregation, istighfar, Ayat al-Kursi, al-Mu'awwidhat, tasbihat.
These are ordered as they appear in the text.
2
Locate the proof for each act
For each act, note the hadith or Quranic citation provided. For example, the imam's turning is based on the practice of the Prophet as recorded in Bukhari and Muslim.
Some proofs are explicit, others are general.
3
Determine the ruling level
Use the commentary to classify each act as sunnah muakkadah. The text consistently uses 'yustahabb' (recommended) and emphasizes the prophetic proof.
None of these are wajib; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer.
4
Analyze differences in order and numbers
The passage discusses variations in the sequence of tasbihat and the numbers reported in hadith. Understand that these differences indicate flexibility and that any form is acceptable.
Most scholars restrict tasbihat to obligatory prayers, as indicated by the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi position
Combine the information to state the Hanafi operative ruling: these acts are sunnah muakkadah, the order of tasbihat is flexible, and the numbers can vary from 11 to 100 per set.
The Hanafi school relies on the more comprehensive narrations.

And for increasing his witnesses due to what is narrated that the place of the worshipper will testify for him on the Day of Judgement. And it is recommended that after it (i.e., after the supererogatory prayer), and immediately after the obligatory prayer if there is no supererogatory prayer after it, he faces the people if he wishes, provided he is not opposite someone praying. Because in the two Sahihs: When the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed, he turned his face towards us. And if the imam wishes, he may turn to his left, placing the qibla to his right; and if he wishes, he may turn to his right, placing the qibla to his left. This is preferable because in Muslim: When we prayed behind the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), we loved to be on his right so that he would turn his face towards us. And if he wishes, he may go for his needs. Allah said: 'And when the prayer is concluded, disperse through the land and seek of Allah's bounty.' The command is for permissibility. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: When he finishes his prayer, if he wishes he may recite his wird sitting, and if he wishes he may recite it standing. And they seek forgiveness from Allah, the Mighty, thrice, due to the saying of Thawban: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), when he finished his prayer, would seek forgiveness from Allah thrice and say: 'O Allah, You are Peace and from You is peace, blessed are You, O Possessor of majesty and honor.' Reported by Muslim. And he (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever seeks forgiveness from Allah after every prayer three times, saying: 'I seek forgiveness from Allah, besides Whom there is no god, the Living, the Self-Subsisting, and I repent to Him,' his sins will be forgiven even if he fled from the battle line.' And they recite Ayat al-Kursi, due to the saying of the Prophet (ﷺ): 'Whoever recites Ayat al-Kursi after every prayer, nothing prevents him from entering Paradise except death. And whoever recites it when he goes to his bed, Allah will protect his house and the house of his neighbor and the people of the small dwellings around him.' And they recite al-Mu'awwidhat, due to the saying of 'Uqba ibn 'Amir (may Allah be pleased with him): 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) ordered me to recite al-Mu'awwidhat after every prayer.' And they glorify Allah (subhanallah) thirty-three times, and praise Him (alhamdulillah) thirty-three times, and magnify Him (allahu akbar) thirty-three times, then they say (to complete one hundred): 'There is no god but Allah, alone, without partner, to Him belongs the kingdom and to Him is praise, and He is over all things competent.' Due to his saying: 'Whoever glorifies Allah after every prayer thirty-three times, and praises Allah...' The Friday does not negate it being on other days; rather it establishes it by way of indication. His saying: 'After every prayer' indicates that the author means every obligatory prayer. His saying: 'Even if he fled from the battle line' means from the battle line required by Shari'ah, like fighting disbelievers, and 'zahf' is used for 'zahif' (crawler) and what is meant is as above. In the hadith, it indicates that this istighfar expiates major sins because fleeing is among the major sins as in the hadith, and this is a method of some scholars. His saying: 'Nothing prevents him from entering Paradise except death' means that when he dies he enters Paradise; the intended meaning is that his soul settles in it, or the intended meaning of entering is enjoyment, meaning he attains enjoyment of the bliss of Paradise, for the grave is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hell. His saying: 'Allah will protect his house, etc.' means Allah preserves what was mentioned. And it is reported that whoever recites it with the endings of Surah al-Baqarah in a place for three nights, no devil will ever approach him. His saying: 'And they recite al-Mu'awwidhat' – it was previously mentioned that there is a predominant usage, and the intended meaning is al-Samadiyyah (Surah al-Ikhlas) and al-Mu'awwidhatan (Surah al-Falaq and an-Nas). Al-Tabarani narrated in some chains of the hadith of Ayat al-Kursi an addition of 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad.' His action indicates that this mentioned manner does not come from a single hadith; rather it is collected from multiple hadith. His saying: 'Whoever glorifies after every prayer, etc.' includes obligatory and supererogatory, but most scholars restrict it to obligatory because it came in the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah in Muslim with the restriction to the prescribed prayer, so they restricted the absolute to the restricted. And this order occurs in most hadith, and in some narrations the takbir precedes the tahmid specifically, and in one narration the tahmid precedes the tasbih, so that indicates that there is no fixed order in them. It can be said that the preferable is to begin with tasbih because it is of the category of purification (takhliyah), then tahmid because it is of the category of adornment (tahliyah), then takbir because it is magnification. And eleven of each has been reported, and ten, and six, and one, and seventy, and one hundred. So the narrations differ in specifying these numbers, and all of that cannot be except for a wisdom, even if it is hidden from us, so we must comply with that. Al-Hafiz al-Zayn al-'Iraqi said: 'All of that is good, and what is more is more beloved to Allah.' And al-Baghawi reconciled by saying that it is possible that this occurred at different times, and that it is by way of choice, or it differs according to different circumstances as...

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the recommended sunan (mustahabbat) after completing the obligatory prayer. It is a critical refinement by the commentator, building upon the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. The passage covers several distinct but related sunan: the imam's turning to face the congregation, reciting istighfar, Ayat al-Kursi, al-Mu'awwidhat, and the tasbihat (subhanallah, alhamdulillah, allahu akbar 33 times each) followed by the completion phrase (la ilaha illallah...).

The first ruling states that it is mustahabb for the imam, after finishing the prayer (whether obligatory or supererogatory, provided there is no subsequent supererogatory prayer), to turn and face the congregation, provided he is not directly opposite someone who is still praying. The imam has several options: face the people directly, turn left or right (with the qibla to his side), or leave for his needs. The preferred option is based on the hadith in Sahih Muslim where the companions loved to be on the Prophet's right so he would turn to them. The Quranic verse (62:10) is cited as proof of permissibility, as the command to disperse indicates ibahah.

Then the passage discusses the istighfar: it is sunnah to say 'Astaghfirullah' three times after each prayer, based on the hadith of Thawban reported by Muslim. The Prophet would say this and then the supplication 'Allahumma anta as-salam...'. Another hadith promises forgiveness of sins, even major sins like fleeing from battle, for one who recites the longer form of istighfar after each prayer.

Next, the recitation of Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) after each prayer is recommended, with a hadith stating that nothing prevents its reciter from entering Paradise except death. The commentary clarifies that this means the person will enter Paradise immediately upon death, either in soul or in the enjoyment of bliss. Additionally, protection for one's house and neighbors is promised for those who recite it before sleep.

Reciting al-Mu'awwidhat (Surah al-Ikhlas, al-Falaq, an-Nas) after each prayer is also sunnah, based on the command from the Prophet to 'Uqba ibn 'Amir. The commentator notes that these are from multiple hadith and not found in a single narration.

Finally, the tasbihat: saying 'Subhanallah', 'Alhamdulillah', and 'Allahu Akbar' each 33 times, completing with the tahleel (la ilaha illallah) to reach 100. This is supported by the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah in Muslim, which restricts it to obligatory prayers (maktubah). Most scholars interpret the absolute mention in other hadith as referring to obligatory prayers. There is no fixed order for the tasbihat, as narrations vary in sequence. Some scholars recommend starting with tasbih (purity), then tahmid (praise), then takbir (magnification). The numbers also vary in different narrations (11, 10, 6, 1, 70, 100), each having wisdom. The consensus is that any of these forms is good, and increasing is better. The passage emphasizes compliance with these sunan despite varying reports.

Overall, the passage serves to compile and validate the post-prayer adhkar with their prophetic proofs, noting that the combination is from multiple hadith, and addressing issues of order, number, and scope (obligatory vs. supererogatory prayers).

Key Terms
دبر كل صلاة (dubur kulli salat): Immediately after finishing the prayer, whether obligatory or supererogatory, with the understanding most scholars apply it to obligatory prayers specifically.
المعوذات (al-mu'awwidhat): The two refuge-seeking surahs (Surah al-Falaq and an-Nas), sometimes including Surah al-Ikhlas due to a narration, but primarily the two.
تسبيح (tasbih): Saying 'subhanallah' (glory be to Allah), one of the post-prayer dhikr, usually 33 times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on performing the tasbihat (33 times each after prayer)?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
Post-prayer adhkar are sunnah muakkadah; their order and numbers are flexible, and they are primarily recommended after obligatory prayers.
